<span class="i0">The French shall die, and France become a waste.</span>
<span class="i0">Of such good vassals Carle will see the loss."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_77">LXXVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">And came with Esturgant, Estramaris,</span>
<span class="i0">His friend; both wretches, traitors, villains are....</span>
<span class="i0">Thus spake Marsile: "Come forth, Seigneurs; ye both</span>
<span class="i0">To Ronceval's defiles shall go and help</span>
<span class="i0">Me there to lead my host." Both answer: "King,</span>
<span class="i0">At your command, Rollánd and Olivier</span>
<span class="pagenum">[51]</span><span class="i0">Will we assault. No power can the twelve peers</span>
<span class="i0">From death defend against our trenchant swords</span>
<span class="i0">Whose blades shall redden with hot blood. The French</span>
<span class="i0">Are doomed to death and Carle to doleful life.</span>
<span class="i0">France, the Great Land, shall through our arms become</span>
<span class="i0">Your realm. Come, King, to see this verified;</span>
<span class="i0">The Emperor's self a captive we'll present."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_78">LXXVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">There hastens Margariz de Sibilie</span>
<span class="i0">Who holds the country toward the distant sea.</span>
<span class="i0">His beauty such, all ladies are his friends;</span>
<span class="i0">Not one looks on him but to smile, nor can</span>
<span class="i0">Restrain her laughing joy. No Pagan else</span>
<span class="i0">More glorious deeds of chivalry achieved;</span>
<span class="i0">Pressed through the crowd, he cries above the rest</span>
<span class="i0">Unto the king: "Be not dismayed, for I</span>
<span class="i0">To Ronceval will go to kill Rollánd,</span>
<span class="i0">And Olivier shall not escape alive;</span>
<span class="i0">To martyrdom the twelve Peers are condemned.</span>
<span class="i0">See my good sword with gold-embossèd hilt,</span>
<span class="i0">Given me by the <i>Amiralz</i> of Prime;</span>
<span class="pagenum">[52]</span>
<span class="i0">I pledge my faith it will be dyed in blood.</span>
<span class="i0">The French shall perish, France be steeped in shame,</span>
<span class="i0">And Carle the old, with beard all blossom-white,</span>
<span class="i0">Shall see no day uncursed by grief and wrath.</span>
<span class="i0">Before one year we shall have conquered France</span>
<span class="i0">And slept beneath the roofs of Saint-Denis."</span>
<span class="i0">At this, the Pagan king bowed low his head.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_79">LXXIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Next you can see Chernubles de [Val-neire].</span>
<span class="i0">His hair so long, it sweeps the earth, and he</span>
<span class="i0">Can, for his sport, lift greater weight than bear</span>
<span class="i0">Four hundred loaded mules.—In his [far-land]</span>
<span class="i0">They say—the sun ne'er shines, corn cannot grow,</span>
<span class="i0">The rain falls not, the dew wets not the soil;</span>
<span class="i0">No stone there but is black, and it is said</span>
<span class="i0">By some that in that land the demons dwell.</span>
<span class="i0">Thus said Chernubles:—"My sword hangs at my belt;</span>
<span class="i0">At Ronceval I will dye it crimson! should</span>
<span class="i0">I find Rollánd the brave upon my path,</span>
<span class="i0">Nor strike him down, then trust to me no more;</span>
<span class="pagenum">[53]</span><span class="i0">This my good sword shall conquer Durendal,</span>
<span class="i0">The French shall die, and France must be destroyed."</span>
<span class="i0">At these words, rally King Marsile's twelve Peers,</span>
<span class="i0">And lead one hundred thousand Saracens</span>
<span class="i0">Who for the battle hasten and prepare,</span>
<span class="i0">Arming themselves beneath a grove of pines.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_80">LXXX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Pagans put their Moorish hauberks on;</span>
<span class="i0">The greater part are triply lined; they lace</span>
<span class="i0">Their helms of Sarraguce, gird to their thighs</span>
<span class="i0">Swords of Vienna steel; bright are their shields;</span>
<span class="i0">Their lances from Valence; their banners white</span>
<span class="i0">And blue and crimson. Mules and sumpter-beasts</span>
<span class="i0">Are left behind. They mount their battle steeds,</span>
<span class="i0">And forward press in closely serried lines.</span>
<span class="i0">Clear was the day, and brilliant was the sun;</span>
<span class="i0">No armor but reflected back the light.</span>
<span class="i0">A thousand clarions sound their cheering blasts</span>
<span class="i0">So loud, the French can hear—. Says Olivier:</span>
<span class="i0">"Rollànd, companion, hearken! Soon, methinks,</span>
<span class="pagenum">[54]</span><span class="i0">We shall have battle with the Saracens!"</span>
<span class="i0">To which Rollánd: "God grant it may be so.</span>
<span class="i0">Here must we do our duty to our King;</span>
<span class="i0">A man should for his Lord and for his cause</span>
<span class="i0">Distress endure, and bear great heat and cold,</span>
<span class="i0">Lose all, even to his very hair and skin!</span>
<span class="i0">'Tis each man's part to strike with mighty blows,</span>
<span class="i0">That evil songs of us may ne'er be sung.</span>
<span class="i0">The wrong cause have the Pagans, we the right.</span>
<span class="i0">No ill example e'er shall come from me."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<hr style="width: 50%;">
<p><span class="pagenum">[55]</span></p>
<h4>PRELUDE TO THE GREAT BATTLE.</h4>
<h4> <a id="St_81">LXXXI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Olivier from the summit of a hill</span>
<span class="i0">On his right hand looks o'er a grassy vale,</span>
<span class="i0">And views the Pagans' onward marching hordes;</span>
<span class="i0">Then straight he called his faithful friend Rollánd:</span>
<span class="i0">"From Spain a distant rumbling noise I hear,</span>
<span class="i0">So many hauberks white and flashing helms</span>
<span class="i0">I see!—This will inflame our French men's hearts.</span>
<span class="i0">The treason is the work of Ganelon</span>
<span class="i0">Who named us for this post before the King."</span>
<span class="i0">"Hush! Olivier!"—the Count Rollánd replies,</span>
<span class="i0">"'Tis my step-father, speak no other word."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_82">LXXXII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Count Olivier is posted on a hill</span>
<span class="pagenum">[56]</span><span class="i0">From whence Spain's Kingdom he descries, and all</span>
<span class="i0">The swarming host of Saracens; their helms</span>
<span class="i0">So bright bedecked with gold, and their great shields,</span>
<span class="i0">Their 'broidered hauberks, and their waving flags,</span>
<span class="i0">He cannot count the squadrons; in such crowds</span>
<span class="i0">They come, his sight reached not unto their end.</span>
<span class="i0">Then all bewildered he descends the hill,</span>
<span class="i0">Rejoins the French, and all to them relates.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_83">LXXXIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Said Olivier: "I have seen Pagans more</span>
<span class="i0">Than eyes e'er saw upon the earth; at least</span>
<span class="i0">One hundred thousand warriors armed with shields,</span>
<span class="i0">In their white hauberks clad, with helmets laced,</span>
<span class="i0">Lances in rest, and burnished brazen spears.</span>
<span class="i0">Battle ye will have, such as ne'er was before.</span>
<span class="i0">French Lords, may God inspire you with his strength!</span>
<span class="i0">Stand firm your ground, that we may not succumb."</span>
<span class="i0">The French say: "Cursed be those who fly the field!</span>
<span class="i0">Ready to die, not one shall fail you here."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<hr style="width: 50%;">
<p><span class="pagenum">[57]</span></p>
<h4>ROLAND'S PRIDE.</h4>
<h4> <a id="St_84">LXXXIV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Olivier said: "So strong the Pagan host;</span>
<span class="i0">Our French, methinks, in number are too few;</span>
<span class="i0">Companion Rollánd, sound your horn, that Carle</span>
<span class="i0">May hear and send his army back to help."</span>
<span class="i0">Rollánd replies:—"Great folly would be mine,</span>
<span class="i0">And all my glory in sweet France be lost.</span>
<span class="i0">No, I shall strike great blows with Durendal;</span>
<span class="i0">To the golden hilt the blade shall reek with blood.</span>
<span class="i0">In evil hour the felon Pagans came</span>
<span class="i0">Unto the Pass, for all are doomed to die!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_85">LXXXV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">"Rollànd, companion, sound your olifant,</span>
<span class="i0">That Carle may hear and soon bring back the host.</span>
<span class="i0">With all his Baronage the king will give</span>
<span class="pagenum">[58]</span><span class="i0">Us held!"—Replied Rollánd:—"May God fore-fend</span>
<span class="i0">That for my cause my kindred e'er be blamed,</span>
<span class="i0">Or that dishonor fall upon sweet France.</span>
<span class="i0">Nay, I will deal hard blows with Durendal,</span>
<span class="i0">This my good sword now girt unto my side</span>
<span class="i0">Whose blade you'll see all reeking with red blood.</span>
<span class="i0">Those felon Pagans have for their ill fate</span>
<span class="i0">Together met—yea, death awaits them all."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_86">LXXXVI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">"Companion Rollánd, sound your olifant!</span>
<span class="i0">If Carle who passes through the mounts shall hear,</span>
<span class="i0">To you I pledge my word, the French return."</span>
<span class="i0">Answered Rollánd:—"May God forbid!—Ne'er be</span>
<span class="i0">It said by living man that Pagans could</span>
<span class="i0">Cause me to blow my horn, to bring disgrace</span>
<span class="i0">Upon my kin!—When on the battle field,</span>
<span class="i0">I'll strike one thousand seven hundred blows,</span>
<span class="i0">And Durendal all bleeding shall you see.</span>
<span class="i0">[The French are brave and bravely will they strike.]</span>
<span class="i0">Those Spanish Moors are doomed to certain death."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[59]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_87">LXXXVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Olivier said:—"To me there seems no shame;</span>
<span class="i0">I have beheld the Moors of Spain; they swarm</span>
<span class="i0">O'er mountains, vales and lands, hide all the plains;</span>
<span class="i0">Great is this stranger host; our number small."</span>
<span class="i0">Rollánd replies:—"The more my ardor grows.</span>
<span class="i0">God and his [blessed] angels grant that France</span>
<span class="i0">Lose naught of her renown through my default.</span>
<span class="i0">Better to die than in dishonor [live.]</span>
<span class="i0">The more we strike the more Carle's love we gain!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_88">LXXXVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Rollánd is brave and Olivier is wise;</span>
<span class="i0">Both knights of wond'rous courage—and in arms</span>
<span class="i0">And mounted on their steeds, they both will die</span>
<span class="i0">Ere they will shun the fight. Good are the Counts</span>
<span class="i0">And proud their words.—The Pagan felons ride</span>
<span class="i0">In fury on!—"Rollánd," said Olivier,</span>
<span class="i0">"One moment, look! Our foes so close, and Carle</span>
<span class="i0">Afar from us—you have not deigned to blow</span>
<span class="i0">Your horn! If came the king, no hurt were ours.</span>
<span class="i0">Cast your eyes toward the great defiles of Aspre;</span>
<span class="pagenum">[60]</span><span class="i0">There see this most unhappy rear-guard. [Those</span>
<span class="i0">Who here fight, ne'er shall fight on other fields."]</span>
<span class="i0">Rollànd retorts:—"Speak not such shameful words.</span>
<span class="i0">Woe unto him who bears a coward's heart</span>
<span class="i0">Within his breast. There firm shall we remain;</span>
<span class="i0">The combat and the blows from us shall come."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_89">LXXXIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Now when Rollánd the battle sees at hand,</span>
<span class="i0">More than a leopard's or a lion's pride</span>
<span class="i0">He shows. He calls the French and Olivier:</span>
<span class="i0">"Companion, friend, pray, speak of this no more.</span>
<span class="i0">The Emperor who left his French in trust</span>
<span class="i0">To us, has chos'n those twenty thousand men.</span>
<span class="i0">Right well he knows none has a coward's soul.</span>
<span class="i0">A man should suffer hurt for his good lord,</span>
<span class="i0">Endure great cold or scorching heat, and give</span>
<span class="i0">Even to his flesh and blood—Strike with your lance,</span>
<span class="i0">And I with Durendal, my trusty sword,</span>
<span class="i0">Carle's gift. If here I die, may he who wins</span>
<span class="i0">It, say:—'Twas once the sword of a brave knight."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[61]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_90">XC.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Turpin the Archbishop from another side,</span>
<span class="i0">Spurring his courser, mounts a hill and calls</span>
<span class="i0">The French around. This sermon to them speaks:</span>
<span class="i0">"<i>Seigneurs Barons</i>, Carle left us here: for him,</span>
<span class="i0">Our King, our duty is to die, to aid</span>
<span class="i0">In saving Christendom, the Faith of Christ</span>
<span class="i0">Uphold. There, battle will ye have, for there</span>
<span class="i0">Before your eyes behold the Saracens.</span>
<span class="i0">Confess your sins, and for God's mercy pray!</span>
<span class="i0">For your soul's cure I absolution give....</span>
<span class="i0">If you should die, as holy martyrs ye</span>
<span class="i0">Will fall, and places find in Paradise!"</span>
<span class="i0">The French alight and fall upon their knees;</span>
<span class="i0">The Godly Archbishop grants them benison,</span>
<span class="i0">Giving for penance his command to strike.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_91">XCI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The French arise. They stand assoiled and quit</span>
<span class="i0">Of all sins, blessed by Turpin in God's name.</span>
<span class="i0">On swift destriers they mount, armed cap-a-pie</span>
<span class="i0">As Knights arrayed for battle. Count Rollánd</span>
<span class="pagenum">[62]</span>
<span class="i0">Calls Olivier:—"Companion, sire, full well</span>
<span class="i0">You know, it is Count Ganelon who has</span>
<span class="i0">Betrayed us all, and guerdon rich received</span>
<span class="i0">In gold and silver; well the Emp'ror should</span>
<span class="i0">Avenge us! King Marsile a bargain made</span>
<span class="i0">Of us, but swords will make the reck'ning good."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_92">XCII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Through the defiles of Spain hath passed Rollánd</span>
<span class="i0">Mounted on Veillantif, his charger swift</span>
<span class="i0">And strong, bearing his bright and glitt'ring arms.</span>
<span class="i0">On goes the brave Rollánd, his lance borne up</span>
<span class="i0">Skyward, beneath its point a pennon bound,</span>
<span class="i0">Snow-white, whose fringes flap his hand.</span>
<span class="i0">Fair is his form, his visage bright with smiles.</span>
<span class="i0">Behind him follows Olivier his friend;</span>
<span class="i0">The French with joy, him as their champion, hail.</span>
<span class="i0">He on the Heathens throws a haughty glance,</span>
<span class="i0">But casts a sweet and humble look upon</span>
<span class="i0">His French, and to them speaks with courteous tone:</span>
<span class="i0">"<i>Seigneurs Barons</i>, march steadily and close.</span>
<span class="i0">These Pagans hither came to find a grave;</span>
<span class="pagenum">[63]</span><span class="i0">We here shall conquer such great spoil to-day</span>
<span class="i0">As never yet was gained by Kings of France."</span>
<span class="i0">Even as he spoke the word, the armies met.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_93">XCIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Said Olivier:—"No care have I to speak,</span>
<span class="i0">Since you deigned not to blow your olifant,</span>
<span class="i0">All hope of help from Carle for you is lost.</span>
<span class="i0">He knows no word of this; the fault lies not</span>
<span class="i0">In him, nor are yon Knights to blame—ride on</span>
<span class="i0">And gallop to the charge as best you can.</span>
<span class="i0"><i>Seigneurs Barons</i>, recoil not from the foe,</span>
<span class="i0">In God's name! bearing ever this in mind,</span>
<span class="i0">Hard blows to deal and hard blows to endure</span>
<span class="i0">Forget we not the war-cry of King Carle!"</span>
<span class="i0">At this word all the French together shout.</span>
<span class="i0">Who then had heard the cry, "Montjoie!" had known</span>
<span class="i0">What courage is. Then all together rush</span>
<span class="i0">Right onward; God! with what an onset fierce!</span>
<span class="i0">Deeply they spur their steeds for greater speed;</span>
<span class="i0">They burn to fight. What else can they desire?</span>
<span class="i0">The Saracens stand firm and nothing fear....</span>
<span class="i0">Behold the Franks and Pagans hand to hand....</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<hr style="width: 50%;">
<p><span class="pagenum">[64]</span></p>
<h4>THE MELEE.</h4>
<h4> <a id="St_94">XCIV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The nephew of Marsile—his name Aëlroth,</span>
<span class="i0">Forward the first of all spurs on his horse</span>
<span class="i0">Against our French, hurling forth insulting words:</span>
<span class="i0">"To-day, French villains, ye will joust with us;</span>
<span class="i0">Who was to guard you, has betrayed you; mad</span>
<span class="i0">Must be the King who left you in the pass.</span>
<span class="i0">So now the honor of sweet France is lost,</span>
<span class="i0">And Carle the great shall lose his right arm here."</span>
<span class="i0">Rollànd heard.—God! what pain to him! He drives</span>
<span class="i0">His golden spurs into his courser's flanks,</span>
<span class="i0">And rushes at full speed against Aëlroth;</span>
<span class="i0">His shield he breaks, dismails the hauberk linked;</span>
<span class="i0">Cleaving his breast, he severs all the bones,</span>
<span class="i0">And from the spine the ribs disjoint. The lance</span>
<span class="i0">Forth from his body thrusts the Pagan's soul;</span>
<span class="pagenum">[65]</span><span class="i0">The Heathen's corse reels from his horse, falls down</span>
<span class="i0">Upon the earth, the neck cloven in two halves.</span>
<span class="i0">Rollánd still taunts him:—"Go thou, wretch, and know</span>
<span class="i0">Carle was not mad. Ne'er did he treason love,</span>
<span class="i0">And he did well to leave us in the pass.</span>
<span class="i0">To-day sweet France will not her honor lose!</span>
<span class="i0">Strike, Frenchmen, strike; the first sword-stroke is ours;</span>
<span class="i0">We have the right, these gluttons have the wrong!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_95">XCV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Then comes a Duke whose name is Falsarun;</span>
<span class="i0">He is the brother of the King Marsile.</span>
<span class="i0">The lands of Dathan and of Abirun</span>
<span class="i0">He holds: no viler wretch lives under Heaven.</span>
<span class="i0">Vast is his forehead, and the space between</span>
<span class="i0">His deeply sunken eyes is half a foot.</span>
<span class="i0">Seeing his nephew dead, in grief he bounds</span>
<span class="i0">Forth from the serried ranks, and shouts aloud</span>
<span class="i0">The Pagan war-cry, furious 'gainst the French.</span>
<span class="i0">"To-day," he cries, "at last sweet France shall lose</span>
<span class="i0">Her fame!"—When Olivier heard this, in wrath</span>
<span class="i0">He pricks with golden spurs his charger's flanks,</span>
<span class="i0">And, like true baron, lifts his arm to strike,</span>
<span class="pagenum">[66]</span><span class="i0">Shivers the Pagan's shield, his hauberk tears</span>
<span class="i0">Apart. The pennon's folds pass through his breast</span>
<span class="i0">As with the shaft he hurls him from the selle,</span>
<span class="i0">A mangled corpse;—here lies he on the ground.</span>
<span class="i0">Unto the prostrate body Olivier</span>
<span class="i0">Says proudly:—"Wretch, to me thy threats are vain!</span>
<span class="i0">Strike boldly, Franks! The victory shall be ours!</span>
<span class="i0">Montjoie!" he shouts, the battle-cry of Carle.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_96">XCVI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">A king, named Corsablis, from Barbarie,</span>
<span class="i0">A distant land, is there.—The Pagan host</span>
<span class="i0">He calls;—"The field is ours with ease: the French</span>
<span class="i0">So few in numbers we may well disdain,</span>
<span class="i0">Nor Carle shall rescue one; all perish here.</span>
<span class="i0">To-day, they all are doomed to death!" Turpin</span>
<span class="i0">The Archbishop heard him; lived no man on earth</span>
<span class="i0">He hated more than Corsablis; he pricks</span>
<span class="i0">His horse with both his spurs of purest gold,</span>
<span class="i0">And 'gainst him rushes with tremendous force.</span>
<span class="pagenum">[67]</span><span class="i0">The shield and hauberk split; and with a stroke</span>
<span class="i0">Of the long lance into his body driven,</span>
<span class="i0">Corsablis lifeless drops across the path;</span>
<span class="i0">Him, though a corpse, Turpin addresses thus:</span>
<span class="i0">"Thou, coward Pagan, thou hast lied! Great Carl</span>
<span class="i0">My lord, was ever and will ever be</span>
<span class="i0">Our help; and Frenchmen know not how to fly.</span>
<span class="i0">As for thy fellows, we can keep them here;</span>
<span class="i0">I tell you, each this day shall die.—Strike, Franks,</span>
<span class="i0">Yourselves forget not. This first blow, thank God,</span>
<span class="i0">Is ours! Montjoie!" cries he, to hold the field.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_97">XCVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Gerin attacks Malprimis de Brigal</span>
<span class="i0">Whose good shield now was not a denier worth:</span>
<span class="i0">The crystal boss all broken, and one half</span>
<span class="i0">Fall'n on the ground. Down to the flesh Gerin</span>
<span class="i0">His hauberk cleaves, and passes through his heart</span>
<span class="i0">The brazen point of a stout lance. Then falls</span>
<span class="i0">The Pagan chief and dies by that good blow;</span>
<span class="i0">And Sathanas bears off the wretched soul.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[68]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_98">XCVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Gerier, his comrade, strikes the Amurafle,</span>
<span class="i0">Breaks his good shield, his hauberk white unmails,</span>
<span class="i0">Plants in his heart a spear's steel point with such</span>
<span class="i0">Good aim, one blow has pierced the body through;</span>
<span class="i0">And his strong lance-thrust hurls him dead to earth.—</span>
<span class="i0">Said Olivier: "A noble combat ours!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_99">XCIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Duke Sansun rushes on the Almazour;</span>
<span class="i0">He splits the shield with painted flowers and gold</span>
<span class="i0">Embossed. The strong-mailed hauberk shelters not,</span>
<span class="i0">As he is pierced through liver, heart and lungs.</span>
<span class="i0">For him may mourn who will—death-struck he falls:</span>
<span class="i0">"That is a Baron's stroke!" the Archbishop cries.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_100">C.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Anseïs gives his steed the rein, and charges</span>
<span class="i0">Fierce on Turgis de Turteluse; beneath</span>
<span class="i0">The golden boss asunder breaks the shield,</span>
<span class="pagenum">[69]</span><span class="i0">Rips up the hauberk double-linked; so true</span>
<span class="i0">The thrust, that all the steel passed through his breast.</span>
<span class="i0">With this one blow the shaft has struck him dead.</span>
<span class="i0">Rollánd exclaimed: "The stroke is of a Knight!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_101">CI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Then Engelier, the Gascuin of Burdele,</span>
<span class="i0">Spurs deep his horse, and casting loose the rein,</span>
<span class="i0">Rushes upon Escremiz de Valterne;</span>
<span class="i0">Breaks down the buckler fastened to his throat</span>
<span class="i0">And rends his gorget-mail; full in the breast</span>
<span class="i0">The lance strikes deep and passes in between</span>
<span class="i0">The collar bones; dead from the saddle struck</span>
<span class="i0">He falls.—And Turpin says: "Ye all are lost!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_102">CII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Othon assails a Pagan, Estorgant,</span>
<span class="i0">His thrust hits hard the leather of the shield,</span>
<span class="i0">Effacing its bright colors red and white,</span>
<span class="i0">Breaks in his hauberk's sides, and plunges deep</span>
<span class="i0">Within his heart a strong and trenchant spear,</span>
<span class="i0">From off the flying steed striking him dead.</span>
<span class="i0">This done, he says:—"No hope for you remains!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[70]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_103">CIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">And Berengier smites now Estramaris,</span>
<span class="i0">Splits down his shield, shivers his coat of mail</span>
<span class="i0">In shreds and through his bosom drives a lance.</span>
<span class="i0">Dead 'midst one thousand Saracens he drops.</span>
<span class="i0">Of their twelve Peers now ten have breathed their last:</span>
<span class="i0">Chernuble—Margariz, the Count, survive.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_104">CIV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Most valiant Knight is Margariz. 'Mid all</span>
<span class="i0">Beauteous, strong, slender, quick of hand. He spurs</span>
<span class="i0">His horse and charges Olivier; beneath</span>
<span class="i0">The boss of purest gold his shield breaks down,</span>
<span class="i0">Then at his side a pointed lance he aims;</span>
<span class="i0">But God protects him, for the blow ne'er reached</span>
<span class="i0">The flesh. The point grazed only, wounding not.</span>
<span class="i0">Then Margariz unhindered rides away</span>
<span class="i0">And sounds his horn to rally his own men.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_105">CV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The battle rages fierce. All men engage.</span>
<span class="i0">Rollánd, the dauntless, combats with his lance</span>
<span class="pagenum">[71]</span>
<span class="i0">As long as holds the shaft. Fifteen good blows</span>
<span class="i0">It dealt, then broke and fell; now his good sword,</span>
<span class="i0">Loved Durendal, he draws, spurs on his steed</span>
<span class="i0">'Gainst Chernubles, splits his bright helm adorned</span>
<span class="i0">With gems; one blow cleaves through mail-cap and skull,</span>
<span class="i0">Cutting both eyes and visage in two parts,</span>
<span class="i0">And the white hauberk with its close-linked mail;</span>
<span class="i0">Down to the body's fork, the saddle all</span>
<span class="i0">Of beaten gold, still deeper goes the sword,</span>
<span class="i0">Cuts through the courser's chine, nor seeks the joint.</span>
<span class="i0">Upon the verdant grass fall dead both knight</span>
<span class="i0">And steed. And then he cries: "Wretch! ill inspired</span>
<span class="i0">To venture here! Mohammed helped thee not....</span>
<span class="i0">Wretches like you this battle shall not win."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_106">CVI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Count Rollànd rides through the battle-field</span>
<span class="i0">And makes, with Durendal's keen blade in hand,</span>
<span class="i0">A mighty carnage of the Saracens.</span>
<span class="i0">Ah! had you then beheld the valiant Knight</span>
<span class="pagenum">[72]</span><span class="i0">Heap corse on corse; blood drenching all the ground;</span>
<span class="i0">His own arms, hauberk, all besmeared with gore,</span>
<span class="i0">And his good steed from neck to shoulder bleed!</span>
<span class="i0">Still Olivier halts not in his career.</span>
<span class="i0">Of the twelve Peers not one deserves reproach,</span>
<span class="i0">And all the French strike well and massacre</span>
<span class="i0">The foe. The Pagans dead or dying fall.</span>
<span class="i0">Cries the Archbishop: "Well done, Knights of France!</span>
<span class="i0">Montjoie! Montjoie! It is Carle's battle cry!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_107">CVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Olivier grasps the truncheon of his lance,</span>
<span class="i0">Spurs through the storm and fury of the fight,</span>
<span class="i0">And rushes on the Pagan Malsarun,</span>
<span class="i0">Breaks down his shield with flowers and gold embossed,</span>
<span class="i0">Thrusts from their orbs his eyes; his brains dashed out</span>
<span class="i0">Are crushed and trampled 'neath the victor's feet;</span>
<span class="i0">With seven hundred men of theirs he fell.</span>
<span class="i0">The Count next slew Turgis and Estorgus;</span>
<span class="i0">But now the shaft breaks short off by his hand.</span>
<span class="i0">Then said Rollánd: "What mean you, <i>Compagnon</i>?</span>
<span class="pagenum">[73]</span>
<span class="i0">In such a fight as this 'tis not a staff</span>
<span class="i0">We need, but steel and iron, as I deem.</span>
<span class="i0">Where now that sword called Halteclere, with hilt</span>
<span class="i0">Of gold and crystal pommel?" "I lack time</span>
<span class="i0">To draw it," valiant Olivier replies,</span>
<span class="i0">"So busy is my hand in dealing blows!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_108">CVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Lord Olivier then his good sword unsheathed,</span>
<span class="i0">For which Rollánd entreated him so much,</span>
<span class="i0">And showed it to his friend with knightly pride;</span>
<span class="i0">Strikes down a Pagan, Justin de Val-Ferrée,</span>
<span class="i0">Whose head is severed by the blow; cuts through</span>
<span class="i0">Th' embroider'd hauberk, through the body, through</span>
<span class="i0">The saddle all with studs and gold embossed,</span>
<span class="i0">And through the back-bone of the steed. Both man</span>
<span class="i0">And steed fall on the grass before him, dead.</span>
<span class="i0">Rollánd exclaims: "Henceforth, you are indeed</span>
<span class="i0">My brother! These, the strokes loved by King Carle!"</span>
<span class="i0">And echoes round the cry: "Montjoie! Montjoie!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[74]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_109">CIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Count Gerin sits on his horse, Sorel,</span>
<span class="i0">And his companion Gerier, on Passe-Cerf,</span>
<span class="i0">They loose the reins, and both spur on against</span>
<span class="i0">A Pagan, Timozel. One strikes the shield,</span>
<span class="i0">The other strikes the hauberk;—in his heart</span>
<span class="i0">The two spears meet and hurl him lifeless down.</span>
<span class="i0">I never heard it said nor can I know</span>
<span class="i0">By which of them the swifter blow was struck.—</span>
<span class="i0">Esperveris, son to Borel, was next</span>
<span class="i0">By Engelier de Burdele slain. Turpin</span>
<span class="i0">With his own hand gave death to Siglorel</span>
<span class="i0">Th' Enchanter who once entered hell, led there</span>
<span class="i0">By Jupiter's craft. Turpin said:—"Forfeit paid</span>
<span class="i0">For crime!"—"The wretch is vanquished," cried Rollánd,</span>
<span class="i0">"My brother Olivier, such blows I love!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_110">CX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The combat paused not. Franks and Pagans vie</span>
<span class="i0">In dealing blows; attacking now, and now</span>
<span class="i0">Defending. Splintered spears, dripping with blood</span>
<span class="pagenum">[75]</span><span class="i0">So many; o'er the field such numbers strewn:</span>
<span class="i0">Of banners torn and shattered gonfalons!</span>
<span class="i0">So many valiant French mowed in their prime,</span>
<span class="i0">Whom mothers and sweet wives will never see</span>
<span class="i0">Again, nor those of France who in the Pass</span>
<span class="i0">Await them! Carle for these shall weep and mourn.</span>
<span class="i0">But what avails? Naught can he help them now.</span>
<span class="i0">Ill service rendered Ganelon to them</span>
<span class="i0">The day when he to Sarraguce repaired</span>
<span class="i0">To sell his kin. Ere long for this he lost</span>
<span class="i0">Both limb and life, judged and condemned at Aix,</span>
<span class="i0">There to be hanged with thirty of his race</span>
<span class="i0">Who were not spared the punishment of death.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_111">CXI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The battle rages. Wonders all perform;</span>
<span class="i0">Rollánd and Olivier strike hard; Turpin</span>
<span class="i0">Th' Archbishop, deals more than a thousand blows;</span>
<span class="i0">The twelve Peers dally not upon the field,</span>
<span class="i0">While all the French together fight as if</span>
<span class="i0">One man. By hundreds and by thousands fall</span>
<span class="pagenum">[76]</span><span class="i0">The Pagans: none scapes death, save those who fly</span>
<span class="i0">Whether they will or no, all lose their lives.</span>
<span class="i0">And yet the French have lost their strongest arms,</span>
<span class="i0">Their fathers and their kin they will ne'er see</span>
<span class="i0">Again, nor Carle who waits them in the Pass.</span>
<hr class="two">
<span class="i0">Meantime in France an awful scourge prevails:</span>
<span class="i0">Wind, storm, rain, hail and flashing lightning bolts</span>
<span class="i0">Conflict confusedly, and naught more true,</span>
<span class="i0">The earth shook from Saint Michiel-del-Peril</span>
<span class="i0">As far as to the Saints, from Besançon</span>
<span class="i0">Unto the [sea-port] of Guitzand; no house</span>
<span class="i0">Whose walls unshaken stood; darkness at noon</span>
<span class="i0">Shrouded the sky. No beam of light above</span>
<span class="i0">Save when a flash rips up the clouds. Dismayed</span>
<span class="i0">Beholders cry:—"The world's last day has come,</span>
<span class="i0">The destined end of all things is at hand!"</span>
<span class="i0">Unwitting of the truth, their speech is vain....</span>
<span class="i0">'Tis dolour for the death of Count Rollánd!</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_112">CXII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The French [strike] hard; they strike with all their force.</span>
<span class="i0">In multitudes—by thousands die their foes;</span>
<span class="pagenum">[77]</span><span class="i0">Not two out of one hundred thousand now</span>
<span class="i0">Survive. [Turpin] says:—"Brave are all our men;—</span>
<span class="i0">None braver under Heaven—In the Geste</span>
<span class="i0">Of France 'tis writ true vassals have our Kings."</span>
<span class="i0">Seeking their friends, they overrun the field.</span>
<span class="i0">Their eyes are filled with tenderness and tears</span>
<span class="i0">For their dear kindred they so fondly loved....</span>
<span class="i0">Now King Marsile with his great host appears....</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_113">CXIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Marsile advances 'midst a valley deep,</span>
<span class="i0">Surrounded by the mighty host he brought,</span>
<span class="i0">In twenty squadrons mustered and arrayed.</span>
<span class="i0">Bright shine the helmets strewn with gold and gems,</span>
<span class="i0">And shields and hauberks graved. They sound a charge</span>
<span class="i0">With seven hundred clarions sending forth</span>
<span class="i0">Loud blasts throughout the land—Thus said Rollánd:</span>
<span class="i0">"Companion Olivier, my brother, friend,</span>
<span class="i0">The traitor, Ganelon, has sworn our death....</span>
<span class="i0">His treason is too sure; the Emp'ror Carle</span>
<span class="pagenum">[78]</span><span class="i0">For this vile crime will take a vengeance deep.</span>
<span class="i0">A long and cruel battle we shall have,</span>
<span class="i0">Ere this unknown to man. There, I will fight</span>
<span class="i0">With my good Durendal; you, friend, will strike</span>
<span class="i0">With Halteclere—Those noble swords we bore</span>
<span class="i0">Throughout so many lands; such combats won</span>
<span class="i0">By them, vile strains must never chant their deeds."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_114">CXIV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">When the French see the Pagan cohorts swarm</span>
<span class="i0">The country o'er, they call on Olivier,</span>
<span class="i0">Rollánd and the twelve Peers to guard their lives.</span>
<span class="i0">Unto them now the Archbishop speaks his mind:</span>
<span class="i0">"Barons, be not unworthy of yourselves!</span>
<span class="i0">Fly not the field, for God's sake, that brave men</span>
<span class="i0">Sing not ill songs of you! Far better die</span>
<span class="i0">In battle. Doomed, I know, we are to death,</span>
<span class="i0">And ere this day has passed, our lives are o'er.</span>
<span class="i0">But for one thing ye can believe my word:</span>
<span class="i0">For you God's Paradise stands open wide,</span>
<span class="i0">And seats await you 'mid the blessèd Saints."</span>
<span class="i0">These words of comfort reassure the French;</span>
<span class="i0">All in one voice cry out:—"Montjoie! Montjoie!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[79]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_115">CXV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">There was a Saracen from Sarraguce</span>
<span class="i0">Lord of one half the city—Climorin,</span>
<span class="i0">Unlike a Baron; he received the faith</span>
<span class="i0">Of Ganelon, and sealed the treacherous bond</span>
<span class="i0">By pressing on his lip a kiss—Besides</span>
<span class="i0">Unto him gave his sword and carbuncle.</span>
<span class="i0">"I will," said he, "put your great France to shame</span>
<span class="i0">And from the Emperor's head shake off the crown!"</span>
<span class="i0">Mounted on Barbamouche that faster flies</span>
<span class="i0">Than hawk or swallow on the wing, he spurs</span>
<span class="i0">His courser hard, and dropping on its neck</span>
<span class="i0">The rein, he strikes Engelier de Gascuigne;</span>
<span class="i0">Hauberk nor shield is for him a defense:</span>
<span class="i0">Deep in the core the Pagan thrusts his spear</span>
<span class="i0">So mightily, its point comes out behind,</span>
<span class="i0">And with the shaft o'erturns him on the field</span>
<span class="i0">A corse;—he cries. "Fit for destruction these!</span>
<span class="i0">Strike, Pagans, strike, and let us break their lines!"</span>
<span class="i0">The French cry: "God! to lose so brave a Knight!"....</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_116">CXVI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Count Rollánd calls Olivier: "You know,</span>
<span class="i0">Companion, sire, Engelier is no more....</span>
<span class="pagenum">[80]</span><span class="i0">No better Knight had we"—The Count replies:</span>
<span class="i0">"God grant that I avenge him well!" He drives</span>
<span class="i0">His golden spurs into his charger's flanks;</span>
<span class="i0">And waving Halteclere's blood dripping blade,</span>
<span class="i0">The Pagan he assails, and deals a blow....</span>
<span class="i0">O'erthrown is Climorin. The fiends of hell</span>
<span class="i0">Bear off his soul. The Knight then slays the Duke</span>
<span class="i0">Alphaïen, beheads Escababi,</span>
<span class="i0">Unhorses seven Arabs with such skill</span>
<span class="i0">They rise no more to fight. Then said Rollánd:</span>
<span class="i0">"Wroth is my sire, and by my side achieves</span>
<span class="i0">Renown! by such good blows Carl's love is gained.</span>
<span class="i0">Strike, Chevaliers! strike on!"—he cries aloud.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_117">CXVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">From otherwhere is Valdabrun who armed</span>
<span class="i0">Marsile a Knight; lord of four hundred ships.</span>
<span class="i0">There is no sailor but swears by his name;</span>
<span class="i0">'Twas he by treason took Jerusalem,</span>
<span class="i0">Who there the shrine of Solomon profaned,</span>
<span class="i0">And slew before the Fonts the Patriarch;</span>
<span class="i0">'Twas he, received Count Ganelon's vile oath</span>
<span class="i0">And gave him with his sword a thousand marks;</span>
<span class="pagenum">[81]</span><span class="i0">Faster than falcon in its flight his steed</span>
<span class="i0">Named Graminond. He sharply spurs his flanks</span>
<span class="i0">And rushes 'gainst the mighty Duke Sansun,</span>
<span class="i0">Breaks down his shield—the hauberk rends, and thrusts</span>
<span class="i0">Within his breast the pennon of the flag;</span>
<span class="i0">The shaft o'erthrows him from the saddle, dead.</span>
<span class="i0">"Strike Pagans! strike, for we shall conquer them!"</span>
<span class="i0">The French say:—"God! what Baron true we lose!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_118">CXVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">When Count Rollánd sees Sansun lifeless fall,</span>
<span class="i0">You may well know what grief was his. He spurs</span>
<span class="i0">His horse down on the Pagan. Durendal</span>
<span class="i0">More worth than precious gold he lifts to strike</span>
<span class="i0">With all his might; gold studded helm, head, trunk,</span>
<span class="i0">Hauberk asunder cleaves; the blow, e'en through</span>
<span class="i0">The gold boss'd saddle, strikes the courser's back,</span>
<span class="i0">Killing both horse and man. Blame or approve</span>
<span class="i0">Who may. The Pagans say:—"Hard is this blow!"</span>
<span class="i0">Retorts Rollánd:—"For yours no pity can</span>
<span class="i0">I feel—With you the vaunting and the wrong!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[82]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_119">CXIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">An African fresh from the desert land</span>
<span class="i0">Was there, Malquidant, son of king Malcud;</span>
<span class="i0">His armor highly wrought in beaten gold</span>
<span class="i0">Outshines all others in the sun's bright rays.</span>
<span class="i0">Mounted upon his horse named Salt-Perdut,</span>
<span class="i0">He aims a blow at Anseïs' shield, and cuts</span>
<span class="i0">The azure and vermillion all away.</span>
<span class="i0">His hauberk rives asunder, side from side,</span>
<span class="i0">And through his body pass both point and shaft.</span>
<span class="i0">The Count is dead.—His last breath spent and flown.</span>
<span class="i0">The French say:—"Baron, such great woe for you!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_120">CXX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Archbishop Turpin rides across the fields;</span>
<span class="i0">No shaven priest sang ever mass so well</span>
<span class="i0">As he, and showed such prowess in his deeds.</span>
<span class="i0">He to the Pagan:—"May God send all ills</span>
<span class="i0">To thee, who slew the knight my heart bewails!"</span>
<span class="i0">Turpin spurs hard his good steed 'gainst the wretch;</span>
<span class="i0">One blow strikes down his strong Toledo shield:</span>
<span class="i0">The miscreant dead upon the green sward falls.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[83]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_121">CXXI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Elsewhere stands Grandomie who is the son</span>
<span class="i0">Of Capuel king of Cappadoce. He sits</span>
<span class="i0">A steed named Marmorie, than flying bird</span>
<span class="i0">More swift. Loosening the rein, and spurring deep,</span>
<span class="i0">To smite Gerin with all his force he rides;</span>
<span class="i0">Torn from the neck which bears it, shattered falls</span>
<span class="i0">The purple shield, through the rent mail he drives</span>
<span class="i0">The whole blue pennon in his breast. Gerin</span>
<span class="i0">Drops lifeless by this blow, against a rock.</span>
<span class="i0">The Pagan also slays Gerier, his friend,</span>
<span class="i0">And Berengier, and Gui de Saint-Antoine;</span>
<span class="i0">Assailing then the noble Duke Austoire</span>
<span class="i0">Who holds Valence and fiefs along the Rosne,</span>
<span class="i0">He strikes him dead. The Saracens extol</span>
<span class="i0">Their triumph, but how many fall of ours!</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_122">CXXII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Hearing the Frenchmen's sobs, the Count Rollánd</span>
<span class="i0">Grasps in his hand his sword, all reeking blood.</span>
<span class="i0">His mighty heart nigh breaking with his grief,</span>
<span class="i0">Cries to the foe:—"May God all evils send</span>
<span class="pagenum">[84]</span><span class="i0">On thee! him hast thou slain for whom thou shalt</span>
<span class="i0">Most dearly pay!—" He spurs his flying steed....</span>
<span class="i0">Conquer who may—these two fight hand to hand.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_123">CXXIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">A wise and valiant knight was Grandonie,</span>
<span class="i0">Virtuous and fearless vassal. 'Mid his way</span>
<span class="i0">Encountering Count Rollánd, though never seen</span>
<span class="i0">Before, at once he knew 'twas he, as well</span>
<span class="i0">By his proud mien and noble beauty, as</span>
<span class="i0">By his fair countenance and lofty look.</span>
<span class="i0">Awe-struck, despite himself, he vainly tries</span>
<span class="i0">To fly, but rooted to the spot he stays.</span>
<span class="i0">The Count Rollánd smites him so skillfully,</span>
<span class="i0">He splits in two the nazal, helm, nose, mouth,</span>
<span class="i0">And teeth, the body and mailed-armor, then</span>
<span class="i0">Hews through the golden selle, both silver-flaps;</span>
<span class="i0">With a still deeper stroke the courser's back</span>
<span class="i0">Is gashed. So both are slain past remedy.</span>
<span class="i0">The men of Spain cry out all sorrowful;</span>
<span class="i0">But say the French:—"Well our defender strikes."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[85]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_124">CXXIV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Marv'lous the battle, and the tumult fierce;</span>
<span class="i0">The French of strength and fury full, raise high</span>
<span class="i0">Their swords: backs, ribs and wrists are slashed; the flesh</span>
<span class="i0">Cut through rent garments to the quick; along</span>
<span class="i0">The verdant soil the red blood runs in streams.</span>
<span class="i0">The Pagans cry:—"We cannot more endure!</span>
<span class="i0">Great land, Mohammed curse thee!—More than all</span>
<span class="i0">This people bold."—Not one who does not cry</span>
<span class="i0">"Marsile! ride on, O King, thy aid we need!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_125">CXXV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">A battle fierce and wonderful!—Hard strike</span>
<span class="i0">The French with glittering lance, and there you might</span>
<span class="i0">Have seen what miseries man can suffer: Mowed</span>
<span class="i0">And heaped in bloody mounds, all gasping out</span>
<span class="i0">Their lives, some on their backs, some on their teeth—</span>
<span class="i0">The Saracens give way, willing or not;</span>
<span class="i0">By the French lances forced, they fly the field.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[86]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_126">CXXVI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Marsile his warriors massacred beholds,</span>
<span class="i0">And, bidding all his horns and trumpets blow,</span>
<span class="i0">Rides forward, and his whole van rides with him.</span>
<span class="i0">In the van rode a Saracen, Abisme,</span>
<span class="i0">The vilest wretch among his men, sunk deep</span>
<span class="i0">In crimes and shame, who has no faith in God,</span>
<span class="i0">Sainte Marie's son; as black as melted pitch</span>
<span class="i0">His face; more fond of blood and treason foul</span>
<span class="i0">Than of the gold of all Galice. None saw</span>
<span class="i0">Him laugh or play; for courage and rash deeds</span>
<span class="i0">He pleased the vile Marsile whose dragon flag</span>
<span class="i0">He bears. No pity can the Archbishop feel</span>
<span class="i0">For him, and at his sight he craves to try</span>
<span class="i0">His arm, all softly saying to himself:</span>
<span class="i0">"This Saracen is but a heretic;</span>
<span class="i0">Far better die than not to give him death.</span>
<span class="i0">Ne'er cowardice nor coward I endured!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_127">CXXVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Archbishop gives the signal for the fight;</span>
<span class="i0">He rides the horse he captured from Grossaille,</span>
<span class="pagenum">[87]</span><span class="i0">A King he slew among the Danes: a horse</span>
<span class="i0">Of wondrous fleetness, light-hoofed, slender-limbed;</span>
<span class="i0">Thigh short; with broad and mighty haunch; the flanks</span>
<span class="i0">Are long, and very high his spine; pure white</span>
<span class="i0">His tail, and yellow is his mane—his ears</span>
<span class="i0">Are small—light brown his head. This paragon</span>
<span class="i0">Of all the beasts of earth has not his peer.</span>
<span class="i0">The Archbishop, baron-like, spurs on the horse,</span>
<span class="i0">Full bent upon the encounter with Abisme;</span>
<span class="i0">He gains his side and hard he strikes his shield</span>
<span class="i0">Glittering with gems, topaz and amethyst,</span>
<span class="i0">Crystals and carbuncles, which to him gave</span>
<span class="i0">The Emir Galafés—a demon's gift</span>
<span class="i0">To this in Val-Metas. Him Turpin smites</span>
<span class="i0">Nor mercy shows; 'gainst such a blow avails</span>
<span class="i0">The shield but little; sheer from side to side</span>
<span class="i0">Passes the blade ... dead on the place he falls.</span>
<span class="i0">At such exploit amazed, the French exclaim:</span>
<span class="i0">"The archbishop's crosier in his hand is safe!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_128">CXXVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Count Rollánd calls Olivier: "With me,</span>
<span class="i0">Companion, sire, confess that 'mong brave knights</span>
<span class="pagenum">[88]</span><span class="i0">The archbishop upon earth or under Heav'n</span>
<span class="i0">Has not his peer in casting spear or lance."</span>
<span class="i0">Olivier answers:—"To his rescue on!"</span>
<span class="i0">At this the French once more resume the fight.</span>
<span class="i0">Hard are the blows, rough is the strife—Meantime</span>
<span class="i0">The Christian host in greatest sorrow mourn.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_129">CXXIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Whoever could this fight describe? Rollánd</span>
<span class="i0">And Olivier vie with Turpin in skill</span>
<span class="i0">And glorious deeds—The slain can counted be;</span>
<span class="i0">In charts and briefs their numbers are enrolled:</span>
<span class="i0">More than four thousand fell, so says the Geste.</span>
<span class="i0">Four times the French arms were victorious,</span>
<span class="i0">But on the fifth, a cruel fate they met;</span>
<span class="i0">The knights of France found there a grave, except</span>
<span class="i0">Three more whose lives God saved; yet those brave knights,</span>
<span class="i0">Ere falling, their last breath will dearly sell.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<hr style="width: 50%;">
<p><span class="pagenum">[89]</span></p>
<h4>THE HORN.</h4>
<h4> <a id="St_130">CXXX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Seeing so many warriors fall'n around,</span>
<span class="i0">Rollánd unto his comrade Olivier</span>
<span class="i0">Spoke thus: "Companion fair and dear, for God</span>
<span class="i0">Whose blessing rest on you, those vassals true</span>
<span class="i0">And brave lie corses on the battle-field:</span>
<span class="i0">Look! We must mourn for France so sweet and fair,</span>
<span class="i0">From henceforth widowed of such valiant knights.</span>
<span class="i0">Carle, 'would you were amongst us, King and friend!</span>
<span class="i0">What can we do, say, brother Olivier,</span>
<span class="i0">To bring him news of this sore strait of ours!"</span>
<span class="i0">Olivier answers:—"I know not; but this</span>
<span class="i0">I know; for us is better death than shame."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_131">CXXXI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Rollánd says;—"I will blow mine olifant,</span>
<span class="i0">And Carle will hear it from the pass. I pledge</span>
<span class="pagenum">[90]</span><span class="i0">My word the French at once retrace their steps."</span>
<span class="i0">Said Olivier:—"This a great shame would be,</span>
<span class="i0">One which to all your kindred would bequeathe</span>
<span class="i0">A lifetime's stain. When this I asked of you,</span>
<span class="i0">You answered nay, and would do naught. Well, now</span>
<span class="i0">With my consent you shall not;—if you blow</span>
<span class="i0">Your horn, of valor true you show no proof.</span>
<span class="i0">Already, both your arms are drenched with blood."</span>
<span class="i0">Responds the Count:—"These arms have nobly struck."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_132">CXXXII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">"The strife is rude," Rollánd says—"I will blow</span>
<span class="i0">My horn, that Carle may hear."—Said Olivier:—</span>
<span class="i0">"This would not courage be. What I desired,</span>
<span class="i0">Companion, you disdained. Were the king here,</span>
<span class="i0">Safe would we be, but yon brave men are not</span>
<span class="i0">To blame"—"By this my beard," said Olivier,</span>
<span class="i0">"I swear, if e'er I see again sweet Aude,</span>
<span class="i0">My sister, in her arms you ne'er shall lie."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_133">CXXXIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Rollánd asked Olivier—"Why show to me</span>
<span class="i0">Your anger, friend!"—"Companion, yours the fault;</span>
<span class="pagenum">[91]</span>
<span class="i0">True courage means not folly. Better far</span>
<span class="i0">Is prudence than your valiant rage. Our French</span>
<span class="i0">Their lives have lost, your rashness is the cause.</span>
<span class="i0">And now our arms can never more give Carle</span>
<span class="i0">Their service good. Had you believed your friend,</span>
<span class="i0">Amongst us would he be, and ours the field,</span>
<span class="i0">The King Marsile, a captive or a corse.</span>
<span class="i0">Rollànd, your valor brought ill fortune, nor</span>
<span class="i0">Shall Carle the great e'er more our help receive,</span>
<span class="i0">A man unequaled till God's judgment-day.</span>
<span class="i0">Here you shall die, and dying, humble France, ...</span>
<span class="i0">This day our loyal friendship ends—ere falls</span>
<span class="i0">The Vesper-eve, dolorously we part!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_134">CXXXIV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Archbishop heard their strife. In haste he drives</span>
<span class="i0">Into his horse his spurs of purest gold,</span>
<span class="i0">And quick beside them rides. Then chiding them,</span>
<span class="i0">Says:—"Sire Rollánd, and you, Sire Olivier,</span>
<span class="i0">In God's name be no feud between you two;</span>
<span class="i0">No more your horn shall save us; nathless 'twere</span>
<span class="i0">Far better Carle should come and soon avenge</span>
<span class="pagenum">[92]</span><span class="i0">Our deaths. So joyous then these Spanish foes</span>
<span class="i0">Would not return. But as our Franks alight,</span>
<span class="i0">Find us or slain or mangled on the field,</span>
<span class="i0">They will our bodies on their chargers' backs</span>
<span class="i0">Lift in their shrouds with grief and pity, all</span>
<span class="i0">In tears, and bury us in holy ground:</span>
<span class="i0">And neither wolves, nor swine, nor curs shall feed</span>
<span class="i0">On us—" Replies Rollánd:—"Well have you said."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_135">CXXXV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Rollánd raised to his lips the olifant,</span>
<span class="i0">Drew a deep breath, and blew with all his force.</span>
<span class="i0">High are the mountains, and from peak to peak</span>
<span class="i0">The sound re-echoes; thirty leagues away</span>
<span class="i0">'Twas heard by Carle and all his brave compeers.</span>
<span class="i0">Cried the king:—"Our men make battle!—" Ganelon</span>
<span class="i0">Retorts in haste:—"If thus another dared</span>
<span class="i0">To speak, we should denounce it as a lie."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_136">CXXXVI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Count Rollánd in his great anguish blows</span>
<span class="i0">His olifant so mightily, with such</span>
<span class="i0">Despairing agony, his mouth pours forth</span>
<span class="pagenum">[93]</span><span class="i0">The crimson blood, and his swoll'n temples burst.</span>
<span class="i0">Yea, but so far the ringing blast resounds;</span>
<span class="i0">Carle hears it, marching through the pass, Naimes harks,</span>
<span class="i0">The French all listen with attentive ear.</span>
<span class="i0">"That is Rollánd's horn!—" Carle cried, "which ne'er yet</span>
<span class="i0">Was, save in battle, blown!—" But Ganelon</span>
<span class="i0">Replies:—"No fight is there!—you, sire, are old,</span>
<span class="i0">Your hair and beard are all bestrewn with gray,</span>
<span class="i0">And as a child your speech. Well do you know</span>
<span class="i0">Rollánd's great pride. 'Tis marvelous God bears</span>
<span class="i0">With him so long. Already took he Noble</span>
<span class="i0">Without your leave. The Pagans left their walls</span>
<span class="i0">And fought Rollánd, your brave Knight, in the field;</span>
<span class="i0">With his good blade he slew them all, and then</span>
<span class="i0">Washed all the plain with water, that no trace</span>
<span class="i0">Of blood was left—yea, oftentimes he runs</span>
<span class="i0">After a hare all day and blows his horn.</span>
<span class="i0">Doubtless he takes his sport now with his peers;</span>
<span class="i0">And who 'neath Heav'n would dare attack Rollánd?</span>
<span class="i0">None, as I deem. Nay, sire, ride on apace;</span>
<span class="i0">Why do you halt? Still far is the Great Land."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[94]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_137">CXXXVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Rollánd with bleeding mouth and temples burst,</span>
<span class="i0">Still in his anguish, blows his olifant;</span>
<span class="i0">Carle hears it, and his Franks. The king exclaims:</span>
<span class="i0">"That horn has a long breath!" Duke Naimes replies:</span>
<span class="i0">"Rollánd it is, and in a sore distress,</span>
<span class="i0">Upon my faith, a battle rages there!</span>
<span class="i0">A traitor he who would deceive you now.</span>
<span class="i0">To arms! Your war-cry shout, your kinsman save!</span>
<span class="i0">Plainly enough you hear his call for help."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_138">CXXXVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Carle orders all the trumpeters to sound</span>
<span class="i0">The march. The French alight. They arm themselves</span>
<span class="i0">With helmets, hauberks and gold hilted swords,</span>
<span class="i0">Bright bucklers, long sharp spears, with pennons white</span>
<span class="i0">And red and blue. The barons of the host</span>
<span class="i0">Leap on their steeds, all spurring on; while through</span>
<span class="pagenum">[95]</span><span class="i0">The pass they march, each to the other says:</span>
<span class="i0">"Could we but reach Rollánd before he dies,</span>
<span class="i0">What deadly blows, with his, our swords would strike!"</span>
<span class="i0">But what avails?—Too late they will arrive.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_139">CXXXIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The ev'n is clear, the sun its radiant beams</span>
<span class="i0">Reflects upon the marching legions. Spears,</span>
<span class="i0">Hauberks and helms, shields painted with bright flowers,</span>
<span class="i0">Gold pennons all ablaze with glitt'ring hues.</span>
<span class="i0">Burning with wrath the Emperor rides on;</span>
<span class="i0">The French with sad and angered looks. None there</span>
<span class="i0">But weeps aloud. All tremble for Rollánd.</span>
<hr class="two">
<span class="i0">The King commands Count Ganelon be seized</span>
<span class="i0">And given to the scullions of his house.</span>
<span class="i0">Their chief, named Bègue, he calls and bids: "Guard well</span>
<span class="i0">This man as one who all my kin betrayed."</span>
<span class="i0">Him Bègue received, and set upon the Count</span>
<span class="i0">One hundred of his kitchen comrades—best</span>
<span class="pagenum">[96]</span><span class="i0">And worst;—they pluck his beard on lip and cheek;</span>
<span class="i0">Each deals him with his fist four blows, and falls</span>
<span class="i0">On him with lash and stick; they chain his neck</span>
<span class="i0">As they would chain a bear, and he is thrown</span>
<span class="i0">For more dishonor on a sumpter mule,</span>
<span class="i0">There guarded so until to Carle brought back.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_140">CXL.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">High are the mountains, gloomy, terrible,</span>
<span class="i0">The valleys deep, and swift the rushing streams.</span>
<span class="i0">In van, in rear, the brazen trumpets blow,</span>
<span class="i0">Answ'ring the olifant. With angry look</span>
<span class="i0">Rides on the Emp'ror; filled with wrath and grief,</span>
<span class="i0">Follow the French, each sobbing, each in tears,</span>
<span class="i0">Praying that God may guard Rollánd, until</span>
<span class="i0">They reach the battle-field. With him what blows</span>
<span class="i0">Will they not strike? Alas! what boots it now?</span>
<span class="i0">Too late they are and can not come in time.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_141">CXLI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Carle in great anger rides—his snow-white beard</span>
<span class="i0">O'erspreads his breast-plate. Hard the Barons spur,</span>
<span class="pagenum">[97]</span>
<span class="i0">For never one but inwardly doth rage</span>
<span class="i0">That he is far from their great chief, Rollánd,</span>
<span class="i0">Who combats now the Saracens of Spain:</span>
<span class="i0">If wounded he, will one of his survive?</span>
<span class="i0">O God! What Knights those sixty left by him!</span>
<span class="i0">Nor King nor captain better ever had....</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<hr style="width: 50%;">
<p><span class="pagenum">[98]</span></p>
<h4>THE ROUT.</h4>
<h4> <a id="St_142">CXLII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Count Rollánd casts o'er the mounts and vales</span>
<span class="i0">A glance: French corses strew the plains in heaps;</span>
<span class="i0">He for them mourns as gentle chevalier.</span>
<span class="i0">At such a sight the noble hero weeps:</span>
<span class="i0">"Seigneurs, to you may God be merciful!</span>
<span class="i0">To all your souls may He grant Paradise,</span>
<span class="i0">And there may they on beds of heavenly flowers</span>
<span class="i0">Repose!—No better vassals lived! so long</span>
<span class="i0">Have ye served me! So many lands for Carle</span>
<span class="i0">Ye won!—The Emperor for this ill fate</span>
<span class="i0">Has nurtured you!—O land of France, most sweet</span>
<span class="i0">Art thou, but now forsaken and a waste.</span>
<span class="i0">Barons of France, to-day I see you die</span>
<span class="i0">For me; nor can I save or e'en defend</span>
<span class="pagenum">[99]</span><span class="i0">Your lives. Be God your aid, who ne'er played false!</span>
<span class="i0">Olivier, brother, I must not fail thee!</span>
<span class="i0">If other death comes not, of grief I die.</span>
<span class="i0">Come, sire companion ... come to fight again!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_143">CXLIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Soon to the field returns the Count Rollánd</span>
<span class="i0">With Durendal in hand; as a true knight</span>
<span class="i0">He fights. Faldrun del Pin he cleaves in half</span>
<span class="i0">With twenty-four among the bravest foes.</span>
<span class="i0">Never was man so bent upon revenge.</span>
<span class="i0">As run wild deer before the chasing hounds,</span>
<span class="i0">Before Rollánd the Pagans flee.—"Well done!"</span>
<span class="i0">The Archbishop cries, "Such valor a true Knight</span>
<span class="i0">Should have, when mounted, armed, on his good steed!</span>
<span class="i0">Else, not four deniers is he worth: a monk</span>
<span class="i0">In cloister should he be, and spend his life</span>
<span class="i0">In praying for our sins!...." "Strike," said Rollànd,</span>
<span class="i0">"No quarter!"—At the word the French renew</span>
<span class="i0">The combat ... yet the Christian loss was great.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[100]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_144">CXLIV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">When soldiers on the battle-field expect</span>
<span class="i0">No quarter—desperate they fight; and thus</span>
<span class="i0">The French, like lions, fiercely stand at bay.</span>
<span class="i0">Like a true baron King Marsile rides forth</span>
<span class="i0">Upon his steed Gaignon, and spurs him on</span>
<span class="i0">Against Bevum, of Belne and Digun lord,</span>
<span class="i0">His buckler cleaves, his hauberk with a blow</span>
<span class="i0">Shatters, and lays him dead upon the field.</span>
<span class="i0">Then fall beneath the Pagan King, Ivoire</span>
<span class="i0">And Ivun; then Gerard de Roussillon.—</span>
<span class="i0">The Count Rollánd is nigh and cries aloud:</span>
<span class="i0">"God give damnation unto thee who thus</span>
<span class="i0">So foully slay'st my friends! But ere we part,</span>
<span class="i0">Dearly shalt thou abye it, and to-day</span>
<span class="i0">Shalt learn the name my good sword bears."—He strikes</span>
<span class="i0">The King a true Knight's stroke, and his right hand</span>
<span class="i0">Lops at the wrist; then Turfaleu the fair,</span>
<span class="i0">Marsile's own son, beheads. The Pagans say:</span>
<span class="i0">"Aid us, Mahum! Avenge us, Gods of ours,</span>
<span class="i0">On Carle, who brought such villains to our land,</span>
<span class="i0">As rather than depart will die."—And each</span>
<span class="pagenum">[101]</span><span class="i0">To each cries: "Let us fly!"—Upon the word,</span>
<span class="i0">A hundred thousand turn in sudden flight.</span>
<span class="i0">Whoever calls them, ne'er will they return.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_145">CXLV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Alas, it not avails! If Marsile flies,</span>
<span class="i0">His uncle Marganice unhurt remained.</span>
<span class="i0">'Tis he who held Carthage, Alferne, Garnaille,</span>
<span class="i0">And Ethiopia, a land accursed;</span>
<span class="i0">Chief of the Blacks, a thick-nosed, large-eared race.</span>
<span class="i0">Of these he more than fifty thousand leads,</span>
<span class="i0">Who ride on proudly, full of wrath, and shout</span>
<span class="i0">The Pagan war-cry.—"Here," said Count Rollànd,</span>
<span class="i0">"Here shall we fall as martyrs. Well I know</span>
<span class="i0">Our end is nigh; but dastard I count him</span>
<span class="i0">Who sells not dear his life. Barons, strike well,</span>
<span class="i0">Strike with your burnished swords, and set such price</span>
<span class="i0">On death and life, that naught of shame shall fall</span>
<span class="i0">On our sweet France. When Carle, my lord, shall come</span>
<span class="i0">Upon this field, and see such slaughter here</span>
<span class="i0">Of Saracens, fifteen to one of ours,</span>
<span class="i0">Then will he breathe a blessing on his Knights."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<hr style="width: 50%;">
<p><span class="pagenum">[102]</span></p>
<h4>OLIVIER'S DEATH.</h4>
<h4> <a id="St_146">CXLVI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">When sees Rollánd this tribe accursed, more black</span>
<span class="i0">Than ink, with glist'ning teeth, their only gleam</span>
<span class="i0">Of white, he said:—"Truly I know to-day</span>
<span class="i0">We die! Strike, Frenchmen, that is my command."</span>
<span class="i0">And Olivier, "Woe to the laggards," cries.</span>
<span class="i0">These words the French hearts fired to meet the fray.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_147">CXLVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Pagans, when they mark how few the French,</span>
<span class="i0">Are filled with pride and comfort, and they say</span>
<span class="i0">One to the other:—"Their King Carle is wrong!"—</span>
<span class="i0">Upon his sorrel steed sits Marganice;</span>
<span class="i0">Urging him hard with pricking spurs of gold,</span>
<span class="i0">Encounters Olivier—strikes him behind,</span>
<span class="pagenum">[103]</span><span class="i0">Drives his white hauberk-links into his heart,</span>
<span class="i0">And through in front came forth the pointed lance.</span>
<span class="i0">The Kalif cries:—"That blow struck home! Carlmagne,</span>
<span class="i0">For thy mishap, left you to guard the Pass!</span>
<span class="i0">That he has wronged us, little may he boast.</span>
<span class="i0">Your death alone for us a vengeance full!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_148">CXLVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Olivier knows his death-wound. In his hand</span>
<span class="i0">He grasps Halteclere's bright steel, and strikes a blow</span>
<span class="i0">Well aimed upon the Kalif's pointed helm;</span>
<span class="i0">He scatters golden flow'rs and gems in dust.</span>
<span class="i0">His head the trenchant blade cleaves to the teeth,</span>
<span class="i0">And dead the Kalif falls.—"Pagan accursed,"</span>
<span class="i0">He cries, "not here shalt thou say Carle lost aught;</span>
<span class="i0">To wife nor lady shalt thou ever boast</span>
<span class="i0">In thine own land, that thou hast reft from Carle</span>
<span class="i0">One denier's worth, or me or others harmed!"</span>
<span class="i0">And then he called Rollànd unto his aid.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[104]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_149">CXLIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Olivier feels that he is hurt to death.</span>
<span class="i0">No vengeance can suffice him; Baron-like</span>
<span class="i0">He strikes amid the press, cuts shields embossed</span>
<span class="i0">And ashen shafts, and spears, feet, shoulders, wrists</span>
<span class="i0">And breasts of horsemen. He who saw him thus</span>
<span class="i0">Dismember Saracens, corse over corse</span>
<span class="i0">Heap on the ground, would of a vassal true</span>
<span class="i0">Remembrance keep. Nor does he now forget</span>
<span class="i0">The rallying cry of Carle:—"Montjoie!" he cries</span>
<span class="i0">Loudly and clear; then calls Rollánd, his friend</span>
<span class="i0">And compeer:—"Sire companion, stand by me!</span>
<span class="i0">This day our breaking hearts forever part!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_150">CL.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Rollánd looks Olivier full in the face;</span>
<span class="i0">Pale, livid, colorless; pure crimson blood</span>
<span class="i0">Drips from his body, and streams on the earth.</span>
<span class="i0">"God!" cried Rollánd, "I know not what to do,</span>
<span class="i0">Companion, friend, thy courage was betrayed</span>
<span class="i0">To-day; nor will such courage e'er be seen</span>
<span class="pagenum">[105]</span>
<span class="i0">In human heart. Sweet France, oh! how shalt thou,</span>
<span class="i0">As widow, wail thy vassals true and brave,</span>
<span class="i0">Humbled and wrecked! The great heart of King Carle</span>
<span class="i0">Will break!" He spake and on his saddle swooned.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_151">CLI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Behold Rollánd, there, fainting on his steed,</span>
<span class="i0">While Olivier stands wounded to the death.</span>
<span class="i0">So great the loss of blood, his troubled eyes</span>
<span class="i0">See naught afar or near, nor mortal man</span>
<span class="i0">Can recognize. Encount'ring there Rollánd,</span>
<span class="i0">Upon his golden-studded helm he struck</span>
<span class="i0">A dreadful blow, which to the nose-plate cleft,</span>
<span class="i0">And split the crest in twain, but left the head</span>
