<span class="pagenum">[159]</span><span class="i0">Full forty thousand knights. How good their steeds,</span>
<span class="i0">How finely wrought their arms! They stand aloof</span>
<span class="i0">Within a shady vale. With his right hand</span>
<span class="i0">He gives to these his blessing. Joseran</span>
<span class="i0">And Godselmes their appointed leaders are.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_225">CCXXV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Barons of Frise and Flamengs Naimes enrolled</span>
<span class="i0">For the eighth legion. Knights in number more</span>
<span class="i0">Than fifty thousand, men who never yield</span>
<span class="i0">In battle. Thus the king: "My service these</span>
<span class="i0">Will do, Rembalt and Hamon de Galice</span>
<span class="i0">Shall lead them forward in all chivalry."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_226">CCXXVI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Duke Naimes and Joseran the Count equip</span>
<span class="i0">The ninth battalion,—brave among the brave.</span>
<span class="i0">Those warriors from Lorraine and Burgundy:</span>
<span class="i0">In number fifty thousand knights; close helmed,</span>
<span class="i0">In hauberk mailed—a stout short-handled lance</span>
<span class="i0">Each wields. Should Arabs not from combat shrink,</span>
<span class="i0">Lorrains and Bourguignons will deal hard blows;</span>
<span class="i0">Tierri Duke of Argonne will be their chief.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[160]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_227">CCXXVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Barons of France make up the tenth. They are</span>
<span class="i0">One hundred thousand captains 'mong the best;</span>
<span class="i0">Hardy and stout, of features proud, hair flecked</span>
<span class="i0">With gray, and beard all white; in hauberk clad</span>
<span class="i0">And linèd coat of mails, girt with their swords</span>
<span class="i0">Of Spain and France; for shelter, brilliant shields</span>
<span class="i0">With various blazons decked, among them known.</span>
<span class="i0">They mount their steeds and clamor for the fight:</span>
<span class="i0">"Montjoie!" they cry.—Comes now Carlemagne the king!</span>
<span class="i0">Geffrei d'Anjou bears up the oriflamme</span>
<span class="i0">Called Roman once, but since the day Saint Pierre</span>
<span class="i0">Made it a standard, it is named Montjoie.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_228">CCXXVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Emperor Carle dismounts, prostrates himself</span>
<span class="i0">Upon the verdant grass, invoking God</span>
<span class="i0">With eyes uplifted toward the rising sun:</span>
<span class="i0">"O father true, this day be my defense!</span>
<span class="i0">Thy hand it was saved Jonas from the whale</span>
<span class="i0">Within whose body he was swallowed up;</span>
<span class="i0">Thou sparedst too the king of Niniva;</span>
<span class="pagenum">[161]</span><span class="i0">And Daniel didst thou save from cruel pain</span>
<span class="i0">When thrown among the lions. By thy might</span>
<span class="i0">Stood the three children safe in burning flames,</span>
<span class="i0">This day grant also unto me thy love,</span>
<span class="i0">Merciful God! List to my prayer; vouchsafe</span>
<span class="i0">That I avenge my nephew, dear Rollánd!"</span>
<span class="i0">Thus having prayed, he stands erect and marks</span>
<span class="i0">His forehead with the sign of might: Then mounts</span>
<span class="i0">A fleet-hoofed courser. Naimes and Joseran</span>
<span class="i0">Carle's stirrup hold—With buckler on his arm</span>
<span class="i0">And trenchant lance in rest; strength, beauty, grace</span>
<span class="i0">Sat on his countenance and visage fair.</span>
<span class="i0">Then firmly seated on his horse he rides....</span>
<span class="i0">Clarions in rear and front reëcho 'round....</span>
<span class="i0">But above all rings out the olifant.</span>
<span class="i0">Meantime the French weep ... mourning for Rollánd.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_229">CCXXIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Most nobly on the Emp'ror Carle proceeds.</span>
<span class="i0">His long beard flowing o'er his coat of mail,</span>
<span class="i0">And so, for love of him, the knights, whereby,</span>
<span class="pagenum">[162]</span><span class="i0">Are surely known the hundred thousand Franks;</span>
<span class="i0">They march through mountains and o'ertopping peaks,</span>
<span class="i0">Deep vales, defiles of frightful look. At last</span>
<span class="i0">Leaving the narrow pass and wasted land,</span>
<span class="i0">They reach the Spanish bourne and make a halt</span>
<span class="i0">Amid a plain. Meanwhile to Baligant</span>
<span class="i0">Return his vanguard scouts; a Syrian spy</span>
<span class="i0">Heralds the news,—"We saw the proud King Carle.</span>
<span class="i0">His warriors fierce will never fail their King.</span>
<span class="i0">To arms—Within a moment look for fight!"</span>
<span class="i0">Baligant cried:—"Good news for our brave hearts!</span>
<span class="i0">Sound all your trumps and let my Pagans know!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_230">CCXXX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Throughout the camp the drums sonorous beat,</span>
<span class="i0">With bellowing horns and blasts of trumpet clear.</span>
<span class="i0">The Pagans arm themselves, and least of all</span>
<span class="i0">The Emir would th' advance delay—He wears</span>
<span class="i0">A hauberk saffron—'broidered round the sides,</span>
<span class="i0">And clasps his helm with gold and gems inlaid.</span>
<span class="i0">On his left side a sword whereto, in pride,</span>
<span class="i0">He gave a name, as Carle had named his sword,</span>
<span class="pagenum">[163]</span><span class="i0">And called the blade his Precieuse. This name</span>
<span class="i0">Shall be the battle-cry his warriors shout——</span>
<span class="i0">Hangs from his neck a large and spreading shield</span>
<span class="i0">Whose golden boss shines with a crystal ring;</span>
<span class="i0">The strap of silk with rosy 'broidery;</span>
<span class="i0">The lance he bears is named Mallet, the shaft</span>
<span class="i0">Of which so huge, more than a beam it looks,</span>
<span class="i0">And steel so strong, beneath its weight a mule</span>
<span class="i0">Would groan. Upon his steed mounts Baligant;</span>
<span class="i0">His stirrup held by Marcule d'Ultremer.</span>
<span class="i0">Mighty the Emir's stride across the selle;</span>
<span class="i0">Thin-loined, wide-flanked, deep-chested, all his form</span>
<span class="i0">Well molded; broad his shoulders; clear his eye,</span>
<span class="i0">His visage haughty, curls around his brow.</span>
<span class="i0">White as a summer blossom he appears;</span>
<span class="i0">His valor proved by many feats of war.</span>
<span class="i0">God! what a Baron, had he Christian faith!</span>
<span class="i0">He spurs his horse until the crimson blood</span>
<span class="i0">Reddens its flanks, and lightly bounds across</span>
<span class="i0">A mighty chasm full fifty feet in width.</span>
<span class="i0">The Pagans cry:—"He can defend his marche.</span>
<span class="i0">With him none 'mong the French can cross a lance;</span>
<span class="i0">Will they or not, their lives are forfeit now.</span>
<span class="i0">Yea Carle was mad who did not shun the field."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[164]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_231">CCXXXI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Emir, Baron-like, wears on his chin</span>
<span class="i0">A beard as white as summer flower, and gained</span>
<span class="i0">Among the wisest of his creed a fame;</span>
<span class="i0">In battle fierce and proud. His son Malprime</span>
<span class="i0">Of knightly soul, and from his noble race</span>
<span class="i0">Holding a valiant heart and strength of arm,</span>
<span class="i0">Addressed his father:—"Sire, to horse! to horse!</span>
<span class="i0">Against them! I much wonder whether Carle</span>
<span class="i0">We e'er shall meet."—"Yea," answered Baligant,</span>
<span class="i0">"Carle is a valorous knight; his glorious deeds</span>
<span class="i0">Are writt'n, but now his nephew is no more;</span>
<span class="i0">Against our strength no other man's can stand."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_232">CCXXXII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">"Fair son, Malprime," said th' Emir Baligant,</span>
<span class="i0">"Yesterday fell in death the noble knight</span>
<span class="i0">Rollánd, and Olivier the wise and brave,</span>
<span class="i0">And the twelve Peers by Carle so dearly loved,</span>
<span class="i0">With twenty thousand combatants of France;</span>
<span class="i0">Not at a glove's worth hold I all the rest.</span>
<span class="i0">Anon my Syrian messenger reports</span>
<span class="pagenum">[165]</span><span class="i0">The emperor's approach; ten armies Carle</span>
<span class="i0">Has called in close array; the knight who bears</span>
<span class="i0">The olifant, with clear resounding blast</span>
<span class="i0">Leads his companions, riding in the front;</span>
<span class="i0">Together with them fifteen thousand men</span>
<span class="i0">Of France, all bachelors, whom Carle is wont</span>
<span class="i0">To call his children. These as many follow</span>
<span class="i0">Who for the fiercest combat seem prepared."</span>
<span class="i0">Thus said Malprime: "The first stroke I demand!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_233">CCXXXIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">"Fair son," said Baligant, "to you I grant</span>
<span class="i0">Your full request. Against the French at once</span>
<span class="i0">Engage. Let your companions be Torleu</span>
<span class="i0">The Persian King, and Dapamort who rules</span>
<span class="i0">Leutis. If you subdue the vaunting Carle,</span>
<span class="i0">A portion of my kingdom shall you have</span>
<span class="i0">In fief from the Orient to Val-Marchis."</span>
<span class="i0">Responds Malprime: "To you, O sire, all thanks!"</span>
<span class="i0">And stepping forward, he receives the boon.</span>
<span class="i0">This land had once been swayed by King Fleuri,</span>
<span class="i0">But by Malprime was neither ruled nor seen.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_234">CCXXXIV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Emir Baligant rides through the ranks</span>
<span class="i0">Of all his host, escorted by his son</span>
<span class="pagenum">[166]</span><span class="i0">Of giant stature, and the Kings Torleu</span>
<span class="i0">And Dapamort. In line of battle soon</span>
<span class="i0">Stand thirty legions ranked. Countless the knights,</span>
<span class="i0">And fifteen thousand strong the weakest band</span>
<span class="i0">Can number. First are those of Butentrot,</span>
<span class="i0">The next of Misnia: enormous heads</span>
<span class="i0">O'ertop the spine enrooted in their backs,</span>
<span class="i0">Their shaggy bodies bristling with coarse hair</span>
<span class="i0">Like boars; the third, of Nubles and of Blos;</span>
<span class="i0">The legion fourth of Bruns and Esclavos;</span>
<span class="i0">The fifth of Sorbres and Sorz; from the Ermines</span>
<span class="i0">And Mors is formed the sixth; from Jericho</span>
<span class="i0">The seventh, and the eighth from those of Nigre.</span>
<span class="i0">Of Gros the ninth, and from Balide-la-Fort,</span>
<span class="i0">The legion tenth, men never good for aught.</span>
<span class="i0">With strongest oaths the Emir swears aloud</span>
<span class="i0">By all Mohammed's might and body, "Carle</span>
<span class="i0">Of France rides like a madman to his doom,</span>
<span class="i0">For combat we shall have; recoils he not,</span>
<span class="i0">His brow shall never more wear golden crown."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_235">CCXXXV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Ten other legions are arrayed: the first</span>
<span class="i0">Of Canelieux—ill-visaged people, come</span>
<span class="pagenum">[167]</span><span class="i0">Athwart, from Valfuit; Turks the next; the third</span>
<span class="i0">Persians; the fourth, Persians and Pinceneis;</span>
<span class="i0">The fifth from Soltras come and from Avers;</span>
<span class="i0">Englez and Ormaleis make up the sixth;</span>
<span class="i0">The seventh scions are of Samuel's race;</span>
<span class="i0">The eighth from Braise; Esclavers form the ninth;</span>
<span class="i0">As for the tenth, a horde perverse that came</span>
<span class="i0">From Ociant's deserted land—a race</span>
<span class="i0">Not loving God the Lord; ne'er shall you hear</span>
<span class="i0">Of viler breed: their heathen skin as hard</span>
<span class="i0">As iron, whence it is they need no helms</span>
<span class="i0">Nor hauberks mailed—in battle treach'rous fiends.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_236">CCXXXVI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Emir has himself ten legions armed.</span>
<span class="i0">To form the first the giants of Malpruse</span>
<span class="i0">Were summoned; to the second came the Huns;</span>
<span class="i0">The Hungres made the third; Baldise-la-Lungue</span>
<span class="i0">The fourth, and Val-Penuse the fifth; the sixth</span>
<span class="i0">Maruse; the seventh Leuz and Astrimonies;</span>
<span class="i0">The eighth Argoilles; Clarbone the ninth; the tenth</span>
<span class="i0">Formed of the bearded men of Val-Fondé,</span>
<span class="i0">A tribe that never would love God. The songs</span>
<span class="pagenum">[168]</span><span class="i0">Of Geste of France thus thirty legions count:</span>
<span class="i0">A mighty host where many a trumpet blasts.</span>
<span class="i0">Forward, like valiant knights, the Pagans ride.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_237">CCXXXVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Emir, rich and mighty lord, commands</span>
<span class="i0">Before him to display his dragon-flag,</span>
<span class="i0">The standard of Mahum and Tervagant;</span>
<span class="i0">With it Apollo's image, evil god.</span>
<span class="i0">Ten Canelieus about him ride, and cry</span>
<span class="i0">This sermon with loud voice: "Who by our Gods</span>
<span class="i0">Craves to be saved, with the most contrite heart</span>
<span class="i0">Must pray!" And then the Pagans low incline</span>
<span class="i0">Their heads and chins, with brilliant helms bent down</span>
<span class="i0">To earth.—"Now, gluttons, comes your hour to die!"</span>
<span class="i0">Cry out the French; "Confusion be your lot.</span>
<span class="i0">This day, O God of ours, defend King Carle,</span>
<span class="i0">Turn Thou the scale of battle to his side!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_238">CCXXXVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Emir, great in wisdom, called his son</span>
<span class="i0">And the two kings:—"Seigneurs Barons, in front</span>
<span class="pagenum">[169]</span><span class="i0">Ride ye, and all my legions you shall lead;</span>
<span class="i0">Among them only three will I retain,</span>
<span class="i0">But of the best: The first shall be the Turks,</span>
<span class="i0">The second of the Ormaleis composed,</span>
<span class="i0">And third shall be the Giants of Malpruse,</span>
<span class="i0">While those of Occiant shall near me stand</span>
<span class="i0">To set them on King Carle and on his French.</span>
<span class="i0">Should then the Emperor dare measure arms</span>
<span class="i0">With me, struck from its trunk his head shall fall—</span>
<span class="i0">No right has he to other fate than this."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_239">CCXXXIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Both armies are immense; their squadrons bright.</span>
<span class="i0">Between the combatants nor height, nor hill,</span>
<span class="i0">Nor vale, nor wood that shelter could afford;</span>
<span class="i0">Foe looks on foe across the open field.—</span>
<span class="i0">Said Baligant: "My Saracens, to horse!</span>
<span class="i0">Ride forward to the fight!" The battle flag</span>
<span class="i0">Is borne on high by Amboire d'Oliferne,</span>
<span class="i0">And all shout "Precieuse!" The French exclaim:</span>
<span class="i0">"May ye confounded be this day!" Aloud</span>
<span class="i0">Rises their cry "Montjoie!" The Emperor Carle</span>
<span class="pagenum">[170]</span><span class="i0">His trumpets bid resound, and the olifant</span>
<span class="i0">Whose blast 'whelms all. The Pagans say: "Carle's host</span>
<span class="i0">Is fair! Fierce battle shall we have and dire."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_240">CCXL.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Vast is the plain and broad the field. Behold</span>
<span class="i0">Those dazzling helms inlaid with gold and gems,</span>
<span class="i0">Those shields, those coats of mail with saffron edged,</span>
<span class="i0">Those spears and pennons rolled; hearken ye the voice</span>
<span class="i0">Of trumpets blowing clear and strong, and hark</span>
<span class="i0">The olifant's shrill blast, which sounds the charge.</span>
<span class="i0">The Emir calls his brother, Canabeu,</span>
<span class="i0">The King of Floredée, who rules the land</span>
<span class="i0">As far as Val-Sevrée, and points to Carle's</span>
<span class="i0">Ten must'ring legions: "See the pride of France</span>
<span class="i0">The praised; amid his bearded knights how proud</span>
<span class="i0">The Emperor rides! O'er their hauberks stream</span>
<span class="i0">Their beards as white as snow upon the frost.</span>
<span class="i0">Forsooth! These valiant warriors will strike hard</span>
<span class="i0">With lance and sword, and such a fight be ours</span>
<span class="i0">As never man has fought." Then Baligant,</span>
<span class="i0">Urging his courser further than a man</span>
<span class="pagenum">[171]</span>
<span class="i0">Can hurl a staff, gave reasons and their proof:</span>
<span class="i0">"Come forward, Pagans; follow where I go!"</span>
<span class="i0">Brandishing high the shaft of his own lance,</span>
<span class="i0">At Carle he levels fair its trenchant steel.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_241">CCXLI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">When Carle the Emir sees, and with him borne</span>
<span class="i0">The dragon-standard, all the land o'erswarmed</span>
<span class="i0">By Arab warriors, save that space alone</span>
<span class="i0">Held by his host, he cries with loudest voice:</span>
<span class="i0">"Barons of France, in valor great, we know,</span>
<span class="i0">Upon how many fields ye battled! See</span>
<span class="i0">The Pagans! Traitors vile and cowards all;</span>
<span class="i0">Yea, all their law I count no denier worth.</span>
<span class="i0">What care ye, lords, how vast their numbers are?</span>
<span class="i0">Let those who wish to combat follow me!"</span>
<span class="i0">With pointed spurs he pricks his courser's flanks</span>
<span class="i0">And Tecendur four times leaped in the air.</span>
<span class="i0">Cry out the French:—"A valiant King is this!</span>
<span class="i0">Ride forward, Sire, not one will fail you here."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_242">CCXLII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Clear was the day and bright the sun. Both hosts</span>
<span class="i0">Resplendent, their battalions numberless;</span>
<span class="pagenum">[172]</span><span class="i0">The legions in the van already meet</span>
<span class="i0">In fight. Both Counts Rabel and Guineman</span>
<span class="i0">On their fleet coursers' necks have loosed the rein!</span>
<span class="i0">Sharply they spur, and all the Franks dash on</span>
<span class="i0">To deal with trenchant lance their valiant blows.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_243">CCXLIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">A daring Knight is Count Rabel. With spurs</span>
<span class="i0">Of purest gold he pricks his courser's flanks,</span>
<span class="i0">Rushing to smite Torleu the Persian King.</span>
<span class="i0">No shield, no hauberk can such blow withstand.</span>
<span class="i0">The golden spear went through the Pagan's heart</span>
<span class="i0">And mid the brambles of the road has struck</span>
<span class="i0">Him dead. The French cry out: "Aid us, O God!</span>
<span class="i0">With Carle the right; ne'er shall we fail our King!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_244">CCXLIV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Guineman 'gainst the King of Leutice tilts;</span>
<span class="i0">The Pagan's shield with painted flowers bedecked</span>
<span class="i0">Is shattered and his hauberk torn away.</span>
<span class="i0">Through his heart's core the pennon of the Knight</span>
<span class="pagenum">[173]</span>
<span class="i0">Is driven, bearing death,—or laugh or weep</span>
<span class="i0">Who may. At such a blow the French exclaim:</span>
<span class="i0">"Barons, strike ever! Strike and be not slack</span>
<span class="i0">Against the Pagan hordes; to Carle belongs</span>
<span class="i0">The right. With us the justice true of God!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_245">CCXLV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Malprime upon a steed of purest white</span>
<span class="i0">Leads 'gainst the serried legions of the Franks</span>
<span class="i0">His men. Abating not his mighty blows,</span>
<span class="i0">Corse over corse he heaps. Cries Baligant</span>
<span class="i0">In front: "Ye whom my kindness nurtured long,</span>
<span class="i0">Barons of mine, see how my son seeks Carle</span>
<span class="i0">And with so many knights he measured arms;</span>
<span class="i0">A better vassal I shall never claim;</span>
<span class="i0">Give him the succor of your trenchant spears."</span>
<span class="i0">On rush the Pagans at these words, and deal</span>
<span class="i0">Their mortal blows around. Rude is the fight!</span>
<span class="i0">The battle marvelous and stern. None such</span>
<span class="i0">Was ever seen before or since that hour.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_246">CCXLVI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The hosts are numberless, the warriors fierce—</span>
<span class="i0">The encount'ring legions fighting hand to hand</span>
<span class="pagenum">[174]</span><span class="i0">Noblest exploits achieved. How many a lance</span>
<span class="i0">Asunder broken; God! How many shields</span>
<span class="i0">In pieces split, how many hauberks wrenched!</span>
<span class="i0">Splinters of shivered armor you might see</span>
<span class="i0">Strew all the field, and verdant tender grass</span>
<span class="i0">Vermillioned o'er by streams of human gore!</span>
<span class="i0">The Emir to his people calls anew:</span>
<span class="i0">"Barons strike down these Christian people!"—Hard</span>
<span class="i0">And long the fight embittered by revenge</span>
<span class="i0">And rage. Ne'er seen before nor will be seen</span>
<span class="i0">Again such combat.—To the death they fight.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_247">CCXLVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Emir to his men:—"Strike, Pagans, ye</span>
<span class="i0">For this alone have come. Dames sweet and fair</span>
<span class="i0">Shall be your guerdon; honors, and domains</span>
<span class="i0">I promise all."—The Saracens respond:</span>
<span class="i0">"To serve you all we ought."—So hard they fight</span>
<span class="i0">That in the hot affray they lose their spears:</span>
<span class="i0">Anon a thousand flashing swords and more,</span>
<span class="i0">Are drawn, a bloody slaughter to achieve.</span>
<span class="i0">He who stood on that field, true battle saw.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[175]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_248">CCXLVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The King exhorts his French: "Beloved Seigneurs</span>
<span class="i0">And trusty Knights, ye many battles fought</span>
<span class="i0">For me, won many a realm, defeated Kings!</span>
<span class="i0">Full well I know, rich guerdons have ye earned;</span>
<span class="i0">My wealth, lands, blood I owe you. Now to-day</span>
<span class="i0">Your sons, your brothers and your kin avenge</span>
<span class="i0">Who fell in Ronceval but yesternight!</span>
<span class="i0">Well know ye mine the right, with them the wrong."</span>
<span class="i0">The French reply:—"Yea, sire, you speak the truth."</span>
<span class="i0">The twenty thousand knights who march with Carle</span>
<span class="i0">Pledge with one soul their fealty. Dire distress,</span>
<span class="i0">E'en death, shall cause not one of these to fail</span>
<span class="i0">The Emperor; not on lances they rely,</span>
<span class="i0">But with the sword in hand wage doughty strife.</span>
<span class="i0">Wondrous the raging battle. Stern the fight.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_249">CCXLIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The brave Malprime has pressed his steed across</span>
<span class="i0">The field, and carried death among the French.</span>
<span class="pagenum">[176]</span><span class="i0">Duke Naimes glanced proudly toward him, and as knight</span>
<span class="i0">In battle fearless met him in career;</span>
<span class="i0">He strikes ... tears off his buckler's leathern top,</span>
<span class="i0">The hauberk cuts in twain, drives through the heart</span>
<span class="i0">The yellow pennon of the spear, and strikes</span>
<span class="i0">Him dead mid seven hundred other knights.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_250">CCL.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">King Canabeus, the Emir's brother, spurs</span>
<span class="i0">His courser on; his crystal-hilted sword</span>
<span class="i0">Unsheathes, and deals Naimes' princely helm a blow</span>
<span class="i0">Which splits the crest in twain; the trenchant blade</span>
<span class="i0">Severs the five strong bands which to his head</span>
<span class="i0">Fast bound it; now not worth a denier was</span>
<span class="i0">The steel-mailed hood; down to the flesh the casque</span>
<span class="i0">Sheer cleft—a fragment falls upon the earth.</span>
<span class="i0">The blow was great; the Duke, astounded, reeled,</span>
<span class="i0">And would have fallen but for God's help. He clasps</span>
<span class="pagenum">[177]</span><span class="i0">His courser's neck, and should the Pagan deal</span>
<span class="i0">Another stroke, the noble Duke has breathed</span>
<span class="i0">His last; but to his help comes Carle of France.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_251">CCLI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">In the Duke Naimes' brave heart what agony!</span>
<span class="i0">Once more the Pagan raised his arm to strike,</span>
<span class="i0">But now King Carle cries:—"Coward, wretch! This blow</span>
<span class="i0">Brings thee ill luck!"—And valiantly the King</span>
<span class="i0">Rushed on, crushed 'gainst his heart the buckler, rent</span>
<span class="i0">The hauberk's top; dead-struck the heathen King</span>
<span class="i0">Falls on the ground ... empty the saddle rests.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_252">CCLII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Deep grief the Emperor felt when there he saw</span>
<span class="i0">Duke Naimes sore-wounded and the verdant grass</span>
<span class="i0">Streamed o'er by his clear blood, and thereupon</span>
<span class="i0">This counsel spoke:—"Fair Naimes, ride close by me;</span>
<span class="i0">The wretch who brought you to this cruel fight</span>
<span class="i0">Has breathed his last, his body by my lance</span>
<span class="pagenum">[178]</span><span class="i0">Transfixed."—The Duke:—"In you my trust, O sire!</span>
<span class="i0">If e'er I live, with knightly service shall</span>
<span class="i0">My arm requite this deed!"—Then side by side</span>
<span class="i0">In faith and love, with twenty thousand knights</span>
<span class="i0">They march. And none of these or flinch or yield.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_253">CCLIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Emir rides across the field, in haste</span>
<span class="i0">To deal a blow against Count Guineman.</span>
<span class="i0">Athwart his heart he breaks the buckler white</span>
<span class="i0">And tears the hauberk's sides apart, disjoints</span>
<span class="i0">Two ribs and hurls him from his courser, dead;</span>
<span class="i0">Then takes the life of Gebain and Lorant,</span>
<span class="i0">And of Richard the old, a Norman Lord.</span>
<span class="i0">The Pagans cry: "<i>Precieuse</i> deserves its name!</span>
<span class="i0">Barons! strike on, Precieuse will save us all!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_254">CCLIV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">A noble sight, those knights of Araby,</span>
<span class="i0">Of Occiant, of Argoille and of Bascle!</span>
<span class="i0">Spears intermix, death to repel or give.</span>
<span class="i0">Nathless the French recoil not from the strife.</span>
<span class="pagenum">[179]</span><span class="i0">On either side they fall heaped high. Till eve</span>
<span class="i0">The storm of battle raged. Meanwhile the knights</span>
<span class="i0">Of France upon that day bore rueful loss;</span>
<span class="i0">Nor stayed the carnage till the day was done.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_255">CCLV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">French and Arabian warriors emulate</span>
<span class="i0">In valor each the other. Ashen shafts</span>
<span class="i0">Break from their brazen heads. Whoso then saw</span>
<span class="i0">Those shields defaced, who heard those hauberks white</span>
<span class="i0">Resound with blows, this dinning clash of shields</span>
<span class="i0">'Gainst helmets grinding, saw those knights and men</span>
<span class="i0">Fall and with dying shrieks roll on the earth,</span>
<span class="i0">Of greatest anguish could the memory keep;</span>
<span class="i0">So fierce this battle raged. The Emir calls</span>
<span class="i0">Upon Apollo, Tervagan, upon</span>
<span class="i0">Mahum: "Till now I served you well, O Gods!</span>
<span class="i0">And I will have an image made for each,</span>
<span class="i0">Molten of purest gold [if ye but help]!"</span>
<span class="i0">Before him then his favorite Gemalfin</span>
<span class="i0">Appears. He brings ill news. "Sire Baligant</span>
<span class="i0">This day brings you mishap; Malprime, your son</span>
<span class="i0">Has fall'n! Your brother Canabeus is dead.</span>
<span class="pagenum">[180]</span><span class="i0">Two Franks the glory have of their defeat,</span>
<span class="i0">One, Carle the Emperor, I deem, so vast</span>
<span class="i0">His fame, his air as <i>Marchis</i> grand, his beard</span>
<span class="i0">As white as April blossom!" At these words</span>
<span class="i0">The Emir's helm declines, his visage sinks</span>
<span class="i0">Low on his breast. Such is his grief, he thinks</span>
<span class="i0">Death nears him. Calling Jangleu d'ultremer,</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_256">CCLVI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Emir said:—"Jangleu, step forth; most wise</span>
<span class="i0">Art thou, thy knowledge great; thy counsel e'er</span>
<span class="i0">I followed; what the chance of victory</span>
<span class="i0">For Franks or Arabs deemest thou?" Jangleu</span>
<span class="i0">Responds:—"Death, Baligant, hangs o'er your head.</span>
<span class="i0">Ne'ermore your gods can save you; Carle is proud,</span>
<span class="i0">And valiant are his men. Ne'er lived a race</span>
<span class="i0">So strong in battle; yet call up your knights</span>
<span class="i0">Of Occiant, Enfruns and Arabs, Turks</span>
<span class="i0">And Giants. Do your duty with all speed."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_257">CCLVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Emir spreads out to the breeze his beard</span>
<span class="i0">As hawthorn blossom white; betide what may,</span>
<span class="pagenum">[181]</span><span class="i0">Escape he will not seek, puts to his lips</span>
<span class="i0">A trumpet clear, whose blast the Pagans hark,</span>
<span class="i0">And fast their cohorts rally on the field.</span>
<span class="i0">They bray and neigh, the men of Occiant,</span>
<span class="i0">While those of Arguile yelp as curs, and charge</span>
<span class="i0">The Franks so rashly, they mow down and break</span>
<span class="i0">Their thickest ranks, and by this blow</span>
<span class="i0">Throw seven thousand dead upon the field.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_258">CCLVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">To Count Ogier is dastardy unknown;</span>
<span class="i0">No better vassal buckled hauberk on.</span>
<span class="i0">When the French legions broken thus he saw,</span>
<span class="i0">He called Tierri Duke of Argonne, Geffrei</span>
<span class="i0">D'Anjou and Jozeran the Count, and spoke</span>
<span class="i0">These haughty words to Carle:—"Behold our men</span>
<span class="i0">By Pagans slaughtered! May God ne'er permit</span>
<span class="i0">Your brow to wear its crown if unrevenged</span>
<span class="i0">Your shame remains!" None dared reply a word,</span>
<span class="i0">But spurring hard their steeds, with loosened reins</span>
<span class="i0">They rush in fury 'gainst the Pagan ranks</span>
<span class="i0">And strike the foes where'er they can be met.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[182]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_259">CCLIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Hard strikes Carlemagne the king, hard strikes Duke Naimes,</span>
<span class="i0">Ogier de Dannemark, Geffrei d'Anjou,</span>
<span class="i0">Who bears the royal pennon. But o'er all</span>
<span class="i0">Ogier de Dannemark puts forth his might;</span>
<span class="i0">He pricks his courser, drops the rein and falls</span>
<span class="i0">Upon the Pagan who the Dragon holds,</span>
<span class="i0">So fiercely, that both Dragon and the King's</span>
<span class="i0">Own flag is crushed before him on the spot.</span>
<span class="i0">When Baligant beholds his gonfalon fall</span>
<span class="i0">And Mahum's flag defenseless, in his heart</span>
<span class="i0">Springs quick the thought, wrong may be on his side</span>
<span class="i0">And right on Carle's. The Pagans [waver now].</span>
<span class="i0">The Emperor Carle around him calls his (Franks):</span>
<span class="i0">"Barons, in God's name, do you stand by me?"</span>
<span class="i0">Respond the French:—"To ask is an offense.</span>
<span class="i0">Accurst be he who deals not glorious strokes!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_260">CCLX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The day wears on and vesper draweth nigh.</span>
<span class="i0">Christians and Pagans, sword in hand, engage;</span>
<span class="pagenum">[183]</span><span class="i0">And valiant are their chiefs, nor mindless they</span>
<span class="i0">Of battle cries:—"Precieuse!" the Emir shouts,</span>
<span class="i0">And Carle:—"Montjoie!" the glorious sign. Each knows</span>
<span class="i0">The other by the clear sonorous voice,</span>
<span class="i0">And 'mid the field encountering, gives and takes</span>
<span class="i0">Fierce blows. Each massy shield receives the shock,</span>
<span class="i0">And each beneath the boss is cloven in twain</span>
<span class="i0">By the strong lance; each hauberk's sides are rent,</span>
<span class="i0">But the keen steel in neither reached the flesh;</span>
<span class="i0">The horse-girths burst and let the saddles fall.</span>
<span class="i0">Dropped to the earth both kings, both to their feet</span>
<span class="i0">Quick springing, dauntlessly unsheathed their swords.</span>
<span class="i0">And now the mortal combat will not cease</span>
<span class="i0">Till Carle or Baligant has fallen in death.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_261">CCLXI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Carle of sweet France is brave, but the Emir feels</span>
<span class="i0">Before him neither fear nor dread. Both wield</span>
<span class="i0">Their naked swords and mighty thrusts exchange.</span>
<span class="pagenum">[184]</span><span class="i0">The shields, of wood and leather multifold,</span>
<span class="i0">Are rent, the nails torn out, the bosses split;</span>
<span class="i0">Each at the other's hauberk aims his blows.</span>
<span class="i0">Both combat breast to breast; the showering sparks</span>
<span class="i0">Wrap both their helms in fire: no end can be</span>
<span class="i0">Till one or other, vanquished, owns his wrong.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_262">CCLXII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Emir said: "King Carle, bethink thee yet;</span>
<span class="i0">Take better counsel with thy heart, and show</span>
<span class="i0">Remorse. Full well I know, by thee my son</span>
<span class="i0">Was slain, thou broughtest ruin through my land.</span>
<span class="i0">Become my man, I will restore [in fief]</span>
<span class="i0">This land [to thee], and to the East, but serve</span>
<span class="i0">Me well." And Carle: "Great shame were that to me!</span>
<span class="i0">To Heathens I can give no peace nor love....</span>
<span class="i0">Receive the law our God revealed; accept</span>
<span class="i0">The faith of Christ.... For e'er my love is thine,</span>
<span class="i0">If thou believe in God, the Almighty King."</span>
<span class="i0">Said Baligant: "Ill words are these of thine:</span>
<span class="i0">[Far better die by the keen edge of sword."]</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[185]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_263">CCLXIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The mighty Emir with a giant's strength</span>
<span class="i0">Smites Carle upon the helm of burnished steel,</span>
<span class="i0">Which splits in twain beneath the ponderous blow,</span>
<span class="i0">Cuts through the silky hair, shears from the scalp</span>
<span class="i0">Fully the breadth of a man's palm and more,</span>
<span class="i0">Baring the skull. Carle staggers, nearly falls,</span>
<span class="i0">But God willed not that he should die or yield.</span>
<span class="i0">Saint Gabriel, with eager flight once more</span>
<span class="i0">Descends, demanding:—"What ails thee, great King?"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_264">CCLXIV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">When Carle the Angel's heavenly accent hears,</span>
<span class="i0">All thought or dread of death forsakes his soul,</span>
<span class="i0">And in him springs again his former strength.</span>
<span class="i0">The Emir by the royal sword of France</span>
<span class="i0">Is struck, his helm all bright with gems is rent,</span>
<span class="i0">His cloven skull pours out the brain, his face</span>
<span class="i0">Is cleft to the very roots of his white beard:</span>
<span class="i0">Dead falls the Pagan past recovery.</span>
<span class="pagenum">[186]</span><span class="i0">Then shouts the King his rallying cry, "Montjoie!"</span>
<span class="i0">Hearing his shout, Duke Naimes hastes up, and brings</span>
<span class="i0">The charger Tecendur for Carle the great</span>
<span class="i0">To mount. The Pagans turn their backs—God wills</span>
<span class="i0">They should not stay. The Franks have their desires.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_265">CCLXV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Pagans fly—such is the will of God;</span>
<span class="i0">Carle leads the French in the pursuit. Thus spake</span>
<span class="i0">The King:—"Seigneurs, the time is come to give</span>
<span class="i0">Vent to just hatred, and your anguished hearts</span>
<span class="i0">Assuage. This very morn I saw your eyes</span>
<span class="i0">Streaming with tears." They cry:—"Our vengeance now!"</span>
<span class="i0">And vying with each other in exploits,</span>
<span class="i0">They deal their mighty blows. But few escape.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_266">CCLXVI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Amidst the sultry heat and clouds of dust</span>
<span class="i0">The Pagans rousèd, by their foes harassed,</span>
<span class="pagenum">[187]</span><span class="i0">Flee far for Sarraguce. To her high tower</span>
<span class="i0">Ascends Queen Bramimunde, where, seeing thus</span>
<span class="i0">The routed Arabs fly, she calls her priests</span>
<span class="i0">And canons, subjects to false law, by God</span>
<span class="i0">Ne'er loved: their crowns no holy tonsure wear.</span>
<span class="i0">She cries aloud:—"Aid us, Mahum! Oh aid!</span>
<span class="i0">O gentle King! Already vanquished are</span>
<span class="i0">Our men, the Emir slain in shameful death!"</span>
<span class="i0">On hearing this, Marsile turned to the wall</span>
<span class="i0">His covered face, and amid bitter tears</span>
<span class="i0">His life departed. Soon the eager fiends</span>
<span class="i0">Bore off to judgment his sin-burthened soul.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_267">CCLXVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Pagans all are slain [or put to flight];</span>
<span class="i0">Carle wins the day. The gates of Sarraguce</span>
<span class="i0">Are stormed, and well he knows, defense is vain.</span>
<span class="i0">He takes the city. All the Christian host</span>
<span class="i0">Pour in, and there repose their limbs this night.</span>
<span class="i0">The King with snow-white beard is filled with pride:</span>
<span class="i0">Queen Bramimunde gives up the citadels;</span>
<span class="i0">Ten of these forts are large, and fifty small.</span>
<span class="i0">Well helped are they whom God Almighty aids.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[188]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_268">CCLXVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The sunny day had passed, the shades of night</span>
<span class="i0">Had fallen; bright the moonlight; all the stars</span>
<span class="i0">In heaven shone. Carle ruled in Sarraguce.</span>
<span class="i0">Unto one thousand men he gave command</span>
<span class="i0">To search throughout the city's synagogues</span>
<span class="i0">And mosques for all their idols and graved signs</span>
<span class="i0">Of gods—these to be broken up and crushed</span>
<span class="i0">By ax and iron mallet he ordains.</span>
<span class="i0">Nor sorcery nor falsehood left. King Carle</span>
<span class="i0">Believes in God and serves him faithfully.</span>
<span class="i0">Then bishops bless the fountains, leading up</span>
<span class="i0">The Heathens to the blest baptismal Font.</span>
<span class="i0">If one perchance resist the King, condemned</span>
<span class="i0">Is he to die, or hanged, or burnt, or slain.</span>
<span class="i0">More than one hundred thousand are baptized</span>
<span class="i0">True Christians; but not so Queen Bramimunde:</span>
<span class="i0">A captive shall she go unto sweet France</span>
<span class="i0">And be converted by the King through love.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_269">CCLXIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Night passes; dawn appears. Carle fortifies</span>
<span class="i0">The towers of Sarraguce. One thousand Knights</span>
<span class="pagenum">[189]</span><span class="i0">Of valor proved are left to guard the town</span>
<span class="i0">In the Emperor's name. With escort strong he rides,</span>
<span class="i0">Followed by Bramimunde a captive, yet</span>
<span class="i0">Commands that naught but kindness she receive.</span>
<span class="i0">In proud and joyous triumph they return;</span>
<span class="i0">Through Nerbune passes the victorious host,</span>
<span class="i0">Unto Burdele, the city great and fair.</span>
<span class="i0">There on the altar of the Baron Saint</span>
<span class="i0">Sevrin, Carle lays the olifant filled full</span>
<span class="i0">Of marks and gold, where pilgrims view it still.</span>
<span class="i0">Passing upon broad skiffs across Girunde,</span>
<span class="i0">To Blaive, he bears the bodies of Rollánd</span>
<span class="i0">And Olivier, his noble <i>Compagnon</i>,</span>
<span class="i0">With the Archbishop good and brave. Beneath</span>
<span class="i0">White monuments he hath the lords entombed</span>
<span class="i0">At Saint-Romain. Here those three Barons lie....</span>
<span class="i0">The French to God and to his saints, once more</span>
<span class="i0">Commend them. Carle anew through mounts and vales</span>
<span class="i0">Proceeds, nor will he stop until in Aix.</span>
<span class="i0">Fast rides he till he nears the marble steps</span>
<span class="i0">Of his great palace; and as soon as reached</span>
<span class="i0">Its tower, by messengers he summons up</span>
<span class="pagenum">[190]</span><span class="i0">Baiviers and Saisnes, Loherencs and Frisons,</span>
<span class="i0">Allemans, Burguignons, Normans, Poitevins,</span>
<span class="i0">Bretons, of France the wisest men; for now</span>
<span class="i0">Ganelon's trial shall have no delay.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<hr style="width: 50%;">
<p><span class="pagenum">[191]</span></p>
<h4>THE PUNISHMENT OF GANELON.</h4>
<hr class="two">
<h4> <a id="St_270">CCLXX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">From Spain at last the Emperor has returned</span>
<span class="i0">To Aix, the noblest seat of France; ascends</span>
<span class="i0">His palace, enters in the stately hall.—</span>
<span class="i0">Now comes to greet him the fair [lady] Aude,</span>
<span class="i0">And asks the King:—"Where is Rollánd the chief</span>
<span class="i0">Who pledged his faith to take me for his wife?"</span>
<span class="i0">Sore-pained, heart-broken, Carle, with weeping eyes,</span>
<span class="i0">Tears his white beard.—"Ah! sister well beloved,</span>
<span class="i0">Thou askest me of one who is no more.</span>
<span class="i0">A worthier match I give thee in exchange;</span>
<span class="i0">Loewis it is. I can not better say.</span>
<span class="i0">He is my son, and will protect my realms."</span>
<span class="i0">Aude answers:—"To my ear these words are strange.</span>
<span class="i0">May God, His saints, His angels, all forfend</span>
<span class="pagenum">[192]</span><span class="i0">That, if Rollánd lives not, I still should live."</span>
<span class="i0">Her color fades, she falls prone at the feet</span>
<span class="i0">Of Carlemagne—dead ... God's mercy on her soul!</span>
<span class="i0">Barons of France mourn her with pitying tears.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_271">CCLXXI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Such was the end of Aude the beautiful.</span>
<span class="i0">The King, in hope 'tis but a swoon, with tears</span>
<span class="i0">And pity taking both her hands, uplifts</span>
<span class="i0">Her form; the head upon the shoulders sinks.</span>
<span class="i0">As soon as Carle knows it is death indeed,</span>
<span class="i0">Four countesses he summons, bids them bear</span>
<span class="i0">In haste the Lady to a nunnery.——</span>
<span class="i0">All night they watched the body, and at morn</span>
<span class="i0">Beside a shrine gently she was entombed</span>
<span class="i0">With highest honors by the King's command.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_272">CCLXXII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">The Emperor is once more at Aix. There stands</span>
<span class="i0">Amid the city 'fore the palace gate,</span>
<span class="i0">In iron chains, the traitor Ganelon.</span>
<span class="i0">His hands are fastened to a stake with thongs</span>
<span class="i0">Of deer-skin by the sergeants who then beat</span>
<span class="pagenum">[193]</span><span class="i0">His body well with staves and heavy cords.</span>
<span class="i0">Such treatment was his true desert. He waits</span>
<span class="i0">His coming doom, in agony of soul.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_273">CCLXXIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Written it is in ancient Geste of France</span>
<span class="i0">That Carle then summoned men from all his lands,</span>
<span class="i0">Who met at Aix's Chapelle. A solemn feast</span>
<span class="i0">It was; some say the Baron Saint Silvestre's.</span>
<span class="i0">This day began the plea and history</span>
<span class="i0">Of Ganelon who wove the treason's plot.</span>
<span class="i0">The Emperor bade them drag him to his bar.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_274">CCLXXIV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">"Seigneurs Barons," said to them Carle the King,</span>
<span class="i0">"Judge Ganelon according to the law.—</span>
<span class="i0">Among my host with me to Spain he came;</span>
<span class="i0">His craft lost twenty thousand of my Franks;</span>
<span class="i0">My nephew, whom ye nevermore shall see,</span>
<span class="i0">And Olivier, the brave and courteous Knight.</span>
<span class="i0">The traitor sold my brave twelve Peers for gain."</span>
<span class="i0">Then Ganelon:—"May I be cursed ere I</span>
<span class="i0">Deny. Of wealth and honors had [Rollánd]</span>
<span class="pagenum">[194]</span><span class="i0">Deprived me, and for this, his loss and death</span>
<span class="i0">I wrought, but treason none I will confess."</span>
<span class="i0">Respond the French:—"On this we counsel take."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_275">CCLXXV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">In presence of the King stands Ganelon</span>
<span class="i0">With bearing hardy, florid countenance;</span>
<span class="i0">Were he but loyal, as a Baron true</span>
<span class="i0">His mien. Upon the French and judges he</span>
<span class="i0">Has cast a glance, and on his thirty kin</span>
<span class="i0">Who 'round him stand; then with firm voice exclaims:</span>
<span class="i0">"Barons! Now hear me all, for love of God!</span>
<span class="i0">I to the Emperor's host belonged, and served</span>
<span class="i0">Him ever in all faith and love. Rollánd,</span>
<span class="i0">His nephew, hatred bore to me, and fain</span>
<span class="i0">Had doomed my days to torture and to death.</span>
<span class="i0">As message-bearer I to King Marsile</span>
<span class="i0">Was sent, wisdom alone my shield and guard;</span>
<span class="i0">I gave defiance to Rollánd the bold,</span>
<span class="i0">To Olivier and to their comrades all:</span>
<span class="i0">By Carle and all his Barons this was heard.</span>
<span class="i0">Revenge this was, but treason it was none."</span>
<span class="i0">Reply the French:—"All this we well shall weigh."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[195]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_276">CCLXXVI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">On seeing the great plea was to commence,</span>
<span class="i0">Thirty good Knights were called by Ganelon</span>
<span class="i0">Out of his kin, and one among them makes</span>
<span class="i0">A speech all others hark: 'tis Pinabel</span>
<span class="i0">Of Castel de Sorence, of greatest skill</span>
<span class="i0">In words, and apt with reason plausible;</span>
<span class="i0">Withal, a vassal brave to guard his arms.</span>
<span class="i0">Thus to him Ganelon:—"In you my trust</span>
<span class="i0">I place; my life from death, my name from shame</span>
<span class="i0">Preserve!"—Said Pinabel:—"Thou shalt be saved.</span>
<span class="i0">Dare one French Knight condemn thee to be hanged,</span>
<span class="i0">And would the Emperor make us both to meet</span>
<span class="i0">In combat, my good sword will his rash word</span>
<span class="i0">Believe."—And at his feet falls Ganelon.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_277">CCLXXVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Baiviers, Saines, Poitevins, Normans and French</span>
<span class="i0">In council met;—Allemans, Tiedeis in great</span>
<span class="i0">Array. Those from Alverne most courteous prove</span>
<span class="i0">And show more kindness unto Pinabel.</span>
<span class="pagenum">[196]</span><span class="i0">One to the others said:—"To leave this plea</span>
<span class="i0">Right would it be, and pray Carl'magne, this once</span>
<span class="i0">To pardon Ganelon who, from this day,</span>
<span class="i0">Will serve his lord with truer faith and love.</span>
<span class="i0">Rollánd lies in his grave; nor wealth, nor gold</span>
<span class="i0">Restores him to your eyes. This cruel fight</span>
<span class="i0">Is folly."—All the Knights approve, save one,</span>
<span class="i0">Tierri, a brother of the Lord Geffrei.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_278">CCLXXVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">To Carle his Barons come again, and say:</span>
<span class="i0">"We pray you, sire, acquit Count Ganelon;</span>
<span class="i0">Then will he serve you with true faith and love.</span>
<span class="i0">Grant him his life which springs from noble race.</span>
<span class="i0">Rollánd lies in his grave; ne'er shall we see</span>
<span class="i0">Him more, nor treasures e'er can bring him back."</span>
<span class="i0">Exclaimed the King: "Vile traitors are ye all!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_279">CLXXIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Now, seeing all will fail him, o'er Carle's eyes</span>
<span class="i0">And features gloom descends; by grief o'erwhelmed</span>
<span class="i0">He cries: "Unhappy that I am!" Then stood</span>
<span class="i0">[Tierri], the brother of Geffrei, the Duke</span>
<span class="pagenum">[197]</span><span class="i0">D'Anjou, before the King. Thin, light of frame,</span>
<span class="i0">Hair raven-black, [face] somewhat brown of hue,</span>
<span class="i0">In height nor tall nor short; with courtesy</span>
<span class="i0">He spake thus to the Emp'ror: "Fair sire King,</span>
<span class="i0">Be not cast down. That I have served you well</span>
<span class="i0">Ere this, you know. 'Tis my ancestral right</span>
<span class="i0">To sit among the judges of the plea.</span>
<span class="i0">However guilty was Rollánd against</span>
<span class="i0">Count Ganelon, his duty to the King</span>
<span class="i0">Should have restrained his hate. A treason foul</span>
<span class="i0">Ganelon wrought against Rollánd; forsworn</span>
<span class="i0">In perjury tow'rd you, he lost himself.</span>
<span class="i0">For all his crimes his death I here demand,</span>
<span class="i0">Death by the cord; his body to the dogs</span>
<span class="i0">Be thrown away—the perjurer's just doom.</span>
<span class="i0">Should any of his kin deny the words</span>
<span class="i0">I speak, this sword of mine girt to my side</span>
<span class="i0">Will make them good."—All cry: "Well have you said."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_280">CCLXXX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Then toward the King advances Pinabel;</span>
<span class="i0">Tall, strong and swift, and brave. Strike he but once,</span>
<span class="i0">No second blow need follow; to the King</span>
<span class="pagenum">[198]</span><span class="i0">He said: "Sire, unto you belongs this plea.</span>
<span class="i0">Command these clamors to be hushed. There stands</span>
<span class="i0">Tierri who now his judgment has pronounced.</span>
<span class="i0">The lie I give him and to fight defy!"</span>
<span class="i0">With this his right hand glove of deer-skin gave</span>
<span class="i0">Unto the King who said: "I must receive</span>
<span class="i0">Good pledges." Of his kin then thirty knights</span>
<span class="i0">Were given as legal sureties of his pledge.</span>
<span class="i0">"I also give my pledge," the Emperor said,</span>
<span class="i0">"And have them guarded safe till judgment pass."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_281">CCLXXXI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">When Tierri sees that now the fight is near,</span>
<span class="i0">He gives the Emperor his right hand glove.</span>
<span class="i0">To him the sureties Carle himself provides,</span>
<span class="i0">Bids that they bring four benches to the place</span>
<span class="i0">Whereon the combatants shall sit. The terms</span>
<span class="i0">Are judged by all the others as most fair.</span>
<span class="i0">Ogier de Dannemarche was chosen to rule</span>
<span class="i0">The lists. Then for their steeds and arms both called.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[199]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_282">CCLXXXII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Both knights now made them ready for the fight,</span>
<span class="i0">Were shriven, assoiled, and blessed; a mass have heard,</span>
<span class="i0">Communion have received, and richest alms</span>
<span class="i0">Bequeathed to monasteries.—Before striking</span>
<span class="i0">They both appear.—Gold spurs their heels adorn;</span>
<span class="i0">They wear white hauberks light and strong; bright helms</span>
<span class="i0">Clasp on their heads, and gold hilt swords are girt</span>
<span class="i0">Upon their thighs, and to their necks are bound</span>
<span class="i0">Strong quartered shields; they wield in each right hand</span>
<span class="i0">A trenchant sword, and on fleet steeds they mount;</span>
<span class="i0">Then melt in tears one hundred thousand knights</span>
<span class="i0">Who for Rollánd's sake wish Tierri well.</span>
<span class="i0">Yea—but God knows what way the thing will end.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_283">CCLXXXIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Beyond the town of Aix a plain extends:</span>
<span class="i0">And here our Barons will the combat try.</span>
<span class="i0">Most valiant knights are both; the steeds they ride</span>
<span class="i0">Are swift and stout; with spurs in flanks, and freed</span>
<span class="i0">Of rein, they dash.—The warriors all their might</span>
<span class="pagenum">[200]</span><span class="i0">And skill unite to strike the surest blow.</span>
<span class="i0">Bucklers beneath the shock are torn and crushed,</span>
<span class="i0">White hauberks rent in shreds, asunder bursts</span>
<span class="i0">Each courser's girth, the saddles, turning, fall.</span>
<span class="i0">One hundred thousand men look weeping on....</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_284">CCLXXXIV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Both knights leap on the earth, and, quick as light,</span>
<span class="i0">Stand face to face.—Strong, fiery Pinabel</span>
<span class="i0">And Tierri for each other seek. Their steeds</span>
<span class="i0">Are fled.—But their gold-hilted swords they wield;</span>
<span class="i0">And on the helms of steel they shower such blows</span>
<span class="i0">As rashed the thongs. Loudly the knights lament,</span>
<span class="i0">And Carle exclaims:—"Show thou the right, O God!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_285">CCLXXXV.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Cried Pinabel:—"Tierri, surrender thou!</span>
<span class="i0">Thy vassal I will be in faith and love,</span>
<span class="i0">And to thy pleasure will I yield my wealth;</span>
<span class="pagenum">[201]</span><span class="i0">But let the King forgive Count Ganelon!"</span>
<span class="i0">Tierri replied:—"Thy offers all are vain;</span>
<span class="i0">Vile treason were it such a pact to make;</span>
<span class="i0">But God shall judge us and make plain the right."</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_286">CCLXXXVI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Then Tierri spake:—"I hold thee, Pinabel,</span>
<span class="i0">As Baron true, great, strong, of handsome mold;</span>
<span class="i0">Thy peers acknowledge thee as valiant knight;</span>
<span class="i0">Well, let this combat cease, between the King</span>
<span class="i0">And thee a covenant I will strive to make.</span>
<span class="i0">On Ganelon such justice shall be done</span>
<span class="i0">That future ages shall record the doom."</span>
<span class="i0">They grasp again their swords and hew</span>
<span class="i0">Each other's gold-encrusted helm with rage</span>
<span class="i0">So rash that sparkling fires spurt through the air.</span>
<span class="i0">No power will now disjoint the combatants:</span>
<span class="i0">The death of one can only close the strife.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_287">CCLXXXVII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">No braver man than Pinabel.—Such blows</span>
<span class="i0">He deals on Tierri's helmet of Provence,</span>
<span class="i0">That the sparks fly in showers, and, falling, set</span>
<span class="pagenum">[202]</span><span class="i0">The grass ablaze. Then aiming at his foe</span>
<span class="i0">His keen-edged brand, down to the brow cuts through</span>
<span class="i0">His helm; the blade glides down across his face,</span>
<span class="i0">And plows his right cheek with a deep red gash;</span>
<span class="i0">Unto his stomach is the haubert rent,</span>
<span class="i0">But God protects him, and averts his death.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_288">CCLXXXVIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Tierri, on seeing blood gush from his brow</span>
<span class="i0">And tinge the grassy field, strikes Pinabel</span>
<span class="i0">On his steel-burnished helmet, and cuts through</span>
<span class="i0">To the nose-plate. His head is cleft in twain</span>
<span class="i0">And gushes forth the brain. This fatal blow</span>
<span class="i0">Gives Pinabel his death, and ends the fight.</span>
<span class="i0">The French exclaim:—"O wondrous work of God!</span>
<span class="i0">Full right it is that Ganelon be hanged</span>
<span class="i0">With all his kin who sureties were for him!"</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_289">CCLXXXIX.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Tierri had won, and on the battle-field</span>
<span class="i0">The Emperor Carle arrived with an escort</span>
<span class="pagenum">[203]</span><span class="i0">Of forty Barons,—Naimes the Duke, Ogier</span>
<span class="i0">De Dannemarche, Geffrei d'Anjou, Willalmes</span>
<span class="i0">De Blaive.—In close embrace the King has pressed</span>
<span class="i0">Tierri, and with his mantle's sables wiped</span>
<span class="i0">The warrior's face; then lays his furs aside</span>
<span class="i0">And on his shoulders others are arrayed.</span>
<span class="i0">Meanwhile the knight, by friendly hands disarmed,</span>
<span class="i0">On an Arabian mule is placed, and so</span>
<span class="i0">This valorous Baron full of joy returns</span>
<span class="i0">To Aix.—Amid the place they all dismount,</span>
<span class="i0">And now the sureties must abide their doom.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_290">CCXC.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Carlemagne around him calls his counts and dukes:</span>
<span class="i0">"What counsel give ye touching those I kept,</span>
<span class="i0">Unto this plea who came for Ganelon</span>
<span class="i0">Themselves sworn hostages for Pinabel?"</span>
<span class="i0">Respond the French:—"Let none of them survive!"—</span>
<span class="i0">Carle then commands a road-keeper, Basbrun:</span>
<span class="pagenum">[204]</span><span class="i0">"Hang them all up on yon accursed tree!</span>
<span class="i0">By this gray beard of mine, I swear, if one</span>
<span class="i0">Escape, thou diest but a villain's death!"—</span>
<span class="i0">Answered the man:—"What else but to obey?"—</span>
<span class="i0">Then by a hundred sergeants roughly seized,</span>
<span class="i0">Those thirty men are hanged.—Who man betrays</span>
<span class="i0">Destroys himself and others drags to death.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<h4> <a id="St_291">CCXCI.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">And now have turned away Baiviers, Allemans,</span>
<span class="i0">Poitevins, Bretons and Normans; but more</span>
<span class="i0">Than all, the French advise that Ganelon</span>
<span class="i0">Should die a death of torture. Then they tie</span>
<span class="i0">With cords his hands and feet. Four sergeants bring</span>
<span class="i0">Four wild and fiery destriers, made mad</span>
<span class="i0">By a mare 'mid the field. A fearful end</span>
<span class="i0">For Ganelon; bound between them, limb from limb</span>
<span class="i0">Is rent away, each nerve and muscle stretched</span>
<span class="i0">And torn. The clear blood streams upon the green.</span>
<span class="i0">Thus perished Ganelon by a felon's death....</span>
<span class="i0">Traitors of evil deeds must never boast.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<p><span class="pagenum">[205]</span></p>
<h4> <a id="St_292">CCXCII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">When the Emperor Carle had wreaked his full revenge,</span>
<span class="i0">He called the bishops from the realms of France,</span>
<span class="i0">And from Baviere, and those of Alemaigne:</span>
<span class="i0">"Now in my [court] have I a captive, sprung</span>
<span class="i0">From noble race. Such sermons has she heard,</span>
<span class="i0">So good examples seen, she will believe</span>
<span class="i0">In the true God, and Christian faith embrace.</span>
<span class="i0">Baptize her so that He may save her soul;</span>
<span class="i0">God-mothers choose her of our noblest dames."</span>
<span class="i0">With a great company the Baths at Aix</span>
<span class="i0">Were thronged, and soon before the holy Fonts</span>
<span class="i0">The Queen received the name of Juliane:</span>
<span class="i0">Henceforth a Christian holding fast the Truth.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<hr style="width: 50%;">
<p><span class="pagenum">[206]</span></p>
<h4>THE END OF THE CHANSON.</h4>
<h4> <a id="St_293">CCXCIII.</a></h4><div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">But when the Emperor had made complete</span>
<span class="i0">His justice and his heavy wrath assuaged,</span>
<span class="i0">And brought Queen Bramimunde to Christian faith,</span>
<span class="i0">The day was over and the night had fall'n.</span>
<span class="i0">The King sought rest within his vaulted room.</span>
<span class="i0">Saint Gabriel brought him word from God and said:</span>
<span class="i0">"Carle, of thy empire summon all the hosts</span>
<span class="i0">For swiftest marching to the land of Bire;</span>
<span class="i0">So shalt thou succor King Vivien in Imphe,</span>
<span class="i0">The city compassed by the Pagan foe.</span>
<span class="i0">The Christians look to thee and cry for help."—</span>
<span class="i0">Will has he none to go, the King, but moans:—</span>
<span class="i0">"O, God," quoth he, "so troublous is my life!"—</span>
<span class="i0">Whereat he weeps, and tears his hoary beard.</span>
<span class="i13">Aoi.</span></div></div>
<hr style="width: 50%;">
<div class="poem"><div class="stanza">
<span class="i0">Thus endeth here the Geste Turoldus sang.</span>
</div></div>
<hr style="width: 50%;">
<h4>FOOTNOTES</h4>
<div class="footnote"><p><a id="Footnote_1"></a><a href="#FNanchor_1" class="pginternal"><span class="label">1</span></a> Molted. Because in that condition, better for hunting.</p></div>
<div class="footnote"><p><a id="Footnote_2"></a><a href="#FNanchor_2" class="pginternal"><span class="label">2</span></a> Pallies. A square piece of silk on which the knights used
to sit. (From Pallium).</p></div>
<div class="footnote"><p><a id="Footnote_3"></a><a href="#FNanchor_3" class="pginternal"><span class="label">3</span></a> Tables. In the romances of the Middle Ages the game of
tables means tric-trac, chess, checkers, etc.</p></div>
<div class="footnote"><p><a id="Footnote_4"></a><a href="#FNanchor_4" class="pginternal"><span class="label">4</span></a> Bezants. A Byzantine coin.</p></div>
<div class="footnote"><p><a id="Footnote_5"></a><a href="#FNanchor_5" class="pginternal"><span class="label">5</span></a> A sort of undergarment made of gold and silk brocade
worn in time of war under the coat of mail, and in time of
peace under the mantle of fur. In the latter case it was of silk.</p></div>
<hr style="width: 50%;">

and meaning on account of their ancient orthography. For more complete
information see Léon Gautier's seventh edition of the text.</p>

<li>
AIX, capital of Charlemagne's empire.  <a href="#St_3" class="pginternal">3</a>.
</li><li>

</li><li>

</li><li>
AMIRALZ, Admiral. <a href="#St_78" class="pginternal">78</a>.
</li><li>
AMURAFLE, from Emir, admiral. <a href="#St_98" class="pginternal">98</a>.
</li><li>

</li><li>

</li><li>
ASTRIMUNIES, Pagan tribes. <a href="#St_236" class="pginternal">236</a>.
</li><li>
BALAGUER, Spanish Arabian city. <a href="#St_73" class="pginternal">73</a>.
</li><li>
BASCLE, Basque--W. Foester, 280. <a href="#St_254" class="pginternal">254</a>.
</li><li>
BELFERNE, Pagan kingdom. <a href="#St_66" class="pginternal">66</a>.
</li><li>
BELNE, Beaune, French city (Burgundy). <a href="#St_144" class="pginternal">144</a>.
</li><li>
BEVUM, man's name--Teutonic. <a href="#St_144" class="pginternal">144</a>.
</li><li>
BIRE and IMPHE, unknown. <a href="#St_293" class="pginternal">293</a>.
</li><li>
BLAVE, Blaye, near Bordeaux, France. <a href="#St_269" class="pginternal">269</a>.
</li><li>
BLOS, Pagan tribe. <a href="#St_234" class="pginternal">234</a>.
</li><li>
BRIGAL, Saracen country. <a href="#St_97" class="pginternal">97</a>.
</li><li>
BRUNS and ESCLAVOS, Teutonic etymology. <a href="#St_234" class="pginternal">234</a>
</li><li>
BRUISE, Prussia. <a href="#St_235" class="pginternal">235</a>.
</li><li>
BUGRE, Bulgarian, and<br>
BUGUERIE, Bulgaria. <a href="#St_174" class="pginternal">174</a>, <a href="#St_211" class="pginternal">211</a>.
</li><li>
<span class="pagenum">{210]</span>BURDELE, Bordeaux. <a href="#St_101" class="pginternal">101</a>.
</li><li>
BUTENTROT, country supposed to be situated in Cappadocia. <a href="#St_234" class="pginternal">234</a>.
<ul><li>
  See P. Meyer in Romania, VII., p. 335.
</li></ul>
</li><li>
CALIFERNE, unknown Pagan country. <a href="#St_211" class="pginternal">211</a>.
</li><li>
CANELIEUS, <a href="#St_236" class="pginternal">236</a>--said to be Chananians by P. Meyer in Romania, VI., p. 477.
</li><li>
CICLATON, Arab silk material. <a href="#St_69" class="pginternal">69</a>.
</li><li>
COMMIBLES, supposed city of Spain. <a href="#St_14" class="pginternal">14</a>.
</li><li>
CLARBONE, imaginary Pagan place. <a href="#St_236" class="pginternal">236</a>.
</li><li>
